2:33:2334:0:14:72:274:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Agglomerative Forces and Cluster Shapes
2:34:2373:14:14:72:278:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:William R. Kerr and Scott Duke Kominers
2:35:2412:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:NBER Working Paper No. 16639
2:36:2440:14:14:72:148:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:December 2010
2:37:2453:14:28:72:240:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:JEL No. J2,J6,L1,L2,L6,O3,R1,R3
2:38:2484:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:39:2492:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:We model spatial clusters of similar firms. Our model highlights how agglomerative forces lead to
2:40:2589:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:localized, individual connections among firms, while interaction costs generate a defined distance
2:41:2687:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:over which attraction forces operate. Overlapping firm interactions yield agglomeration clusters that
2:42:2788:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:are much larger than the underlying agglomerative forces themselves. Empirically, we demonstrate
2:43:2884:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:that our model's assumptions are present in the structure of technology and labor flows within Silicon
2:44:2986:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Valley and its surrounding areas. Our model further identifies how the lengths over which agglomerative
2:45:3089:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:forces operate influence the shapes and sizes of industrial clusters; we confirm these predictions using
2:46:3193:14:42:72:411:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:variations across both technology clusters and industry agglomeration.
2:47:3263:42:14:72:150:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:William R. Kerr
2:48:3278:14:14:72:193:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Harvard Business School
2:49:3301:14:14:72:153:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Rock Center 212
2:50:3316:14:14:72:139:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Soldiers Field
2:51:3330:14:14:72:164:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Boston, MA 02163
2:52:3346:14:14:72:124:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:and NBER
2:53:3354:14:28:72:148:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:wkerr@hbs.edu
2:54:3367:28:14:72:176:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Scott Duke Kominers
2:55:3386:14:14:72:122:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Wyss Hall

3:60:3466:0:28:69:205:699:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:1  Introduction
3:61:3481:28:17:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Agglomerationó industrial clusteringó is a key feature of economic geography. Starting with
3:62:3572:17:17:69:557:654:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Marshall (1920), a large and diverse literature studies why similar Örms often collocate. One
3:63:3665:17:17:69:557:637:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:body of work provides formal theoretical models of di§erent agglomerative forces like technology
3:64:3761:17:17:69:557:620:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sharing or labor pooling among Örms. A second literature measures interactions among Örms
3:65:3850:17:17:69:557:603:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and/or workers directly (e.g., worker moves across Örms, patent citation distances). A third
3:66:3942:17:17:69:557:586:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:literature characterizes di§erences in clustering behavior across industries (e.g., relating R&D
3:67:4038:17:17:69:557:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:intensity to greater spatial concentration). Despite this progress, we have very little understand-
3:68:4137:17:17:69:557:552:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing of the actual connection between micro-level interactions and observed cluster shapes and
3:69:4230:17:17:69:167:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sizes for industries.
3:70:4251:17:17:86:556:518:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This is very worrisome because studies frequently use observed spatial concentrations for
3:71:4340:17:17:69:557:501:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:industries to infer the properties of the underlying forces that cause them. Economists often
3:72:4433:17:17:69:557:484:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:infer that technology spillovers are shorter than labor pooling spillovers because patenting Örms
3:73:4530:17:17:69:557:467:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are relatively more concentrated at the county level than are Örms that use similar types of
3:74:4622:17:17:69:557:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:workers.  Such reasoning, however, clashes with studies which have concluded that spillover
3:75:4713:17:17:69:557:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:e§ects are orders of magnitude stronger over the Örst few city blocks than they are when Örms
3:76:4806:17:17:69:557:416:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are between two and Öve miles apart (e.g., Rosenthal and Strange 2003, 2008, Arzaghi and
3:77:4894:17:17:69:557:399:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Henderson 2008). Many studies Önd that knowledge áows decrease sharply across áoors within
3:78:4984:17:18:69:557:382:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a single building. Why would we believe that we can infer useful information about knowledge
3:79:5076:18:17:69:557:364:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spillovers from the number of patents in a county, when a county averages over 75,000 people in
3:80:5171:17:17:69:130:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:population?
3:81:5182:17:17:86:556:330:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This project examines these issues theoretically and empirically. The core of our work is a
3:82:5273:17:17:69:557:313:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:location choice model that connects limited, localized agglomerative forces with the formation
3:83:5367:17:17:69:557:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of spatial clusters for similar Örms. Agglomerative forces in our model are localized because
3:84:5460:17:17:69:557:279:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örms face interaction costs. Spillover beneÖts exceed these interaction costs at short distances,
3:85:5557:17:17:69:557:262:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:but beyond some distance interaction becomes unproÖtable. For example: while a Örm could
3:86:5645:17:17:69:557:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:learn useful technologies from another Örm 20 miles away, the costs of doing so may be too
3:87:5735:17:17:69:557:228:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:great to justify the e§ort. Clusters are then the product of many small, overlapping regions of
3:88:5830:17:17:69:127:211:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:interaction.
3:89:5842:17:17:86:556:194:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Silicon Valley is the worldís most famous cluster, and many observers credit its success to
3:90:5933:17:17:69:557:177:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:either technology spillovers or labor pooling. Figures 1a and 1b identify the foundations of our
3:91:6029:17:17:69:557:160:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:theoretical framework using technology and labor áows, respectively, in the San Francisco Bay
3:92:6122:17:17:69:557:143:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Area. Figure 1a focuses on technology sourcing in an area surrounding Silicon Valley. Downtown
3:93:6216:17:17:69:557:126:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:San Francisco and Oakland are to the north and o§ of the map. The triangle in the bottom
3:94:6304:17:17:69:557:109:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:right corner of the map is the core of Silicon Valley. This core contains 76% of industrial patents
3:95:6403:17:17:69:539:92:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Öled from the San Francisco Bay Area and 18 of the top 25 zip codes in terms of patenting.
3:96:6493:17:0:86:556:75:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To introduce our model, we describe the primary technology sourcing zones for three of the
4:97:6584:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:four largest zip codes for patenting outside of the core. Each focal zip code is marked with a
4:98:6678:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:star, and the other points of the shape are the three zip codes that Örms in the focal zip code
4:99:6773:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cite most in their work. The orange zone (also labelled with a ì1î) for Menlo Park extends
4:100:6863:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:deepest into the core. The green zone for Redwood City (ì2î) shifts up and encompasses Menlo
4:101:6955:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Park and Palo Alto but less of the core. The black zone for South San Francisco (ì3î) further
4:102:7048:17:17:69:230:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:shifts out and brushes the core.
4:103:7080:17:17:86:556:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These technology zones are characterized by small, overlapping regions. None of the technol-
4:104:7172:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ogy sourcing zones transverse the whole core, much less the whole cluster, and only the closest
4:105:7267:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:zip code (Menlo Park) even reaches far enough into the core to include the area of Silicon Valley
4:106:7364:17:17:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where the greatest number of patents occur. The empirical appendix contains additional maps
4:107:7455:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that show these small, overlapping regions are also evident in the core itself and in other parts
4:108:7552:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the San Francisco region.  While technology sourcing for individual Örms is localized, the
4:109:7645:17:17:69:348:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:resulting cluster extends over a larger expanse of land.
4:110:7701:17:17:86:556:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These properties are also evident in labor áows. Figure 1b describes commuting zones for
4:111:7789:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:scientists and engineers from the 2000 Census of Populations. Zones on the map are approxi-
4:112:7880:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mations, computed from Public Use Micro Area (PUMA) designations. The colored asterisks
4:113:7967:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:indicate locations of work. The zones surrounding the asterisks of similar color indicate the pri-
4:114:8065:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mary PUMAs of residence for the workers. Labor zones are more uniform in direction, with the
4:115:8157:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:star for the work PUMA typically nearer to the center of its labor zone. These labor commuting
4:116:8251:17:17:69:523:376:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:regions again display small, overlapping zones that in turn encompass a large land area.1
4:117:8340:17:17:86:556:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The central construct of our model replicates these features. Our model thus makes explicit
4:118:8431:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that empirical observation of cluster size in the data does not indicate the length of the micro-
4:119:8528:17:17:69:557:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:interactions that produce the cluster. We show, however, that cluster shape and size does depend
4:120:8624:17:17:69:557:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:systematically on whether the localized interactions for Örms in an industry are longer or shorter
4:121:8722:17:17:69:557:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in length. We demonstrate that a longer e§ective spillover region, either due to weaker decay
4:122:8815:17:17:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in beneÖts or lower interaction costs, yields a macro-structure with fewer, larger, and less-dense
4:123:8913:17:17:69:557:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters. These regularities allow researchers to use cluster dimensions to rank order spillover
4:124:9009:17:17:69:360:240:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lengths even though micro-interactions are not observed.
4:125:9065:17:17:86:556:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:After deriving these predictions, we empirically test the model in two ways. We Örst use
4:126:9153:17:17:69:557:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:US patent data to describe di§erences across technology clusters. Patent citations allow us to
4:127:9247:17:17:69:557:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measure e§ective spillover regions by technology. Di§erences in these spillover regions relate to
4:128:9344:17:17:69:557:172:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cluster shapes and sizes as predicted by the model. Technologies with very short distances over
4:129:9439:17:17:69:557:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which Örms interact exhibit clusters that are smaller and denser than technologies that allow for
4:130:9536:17:17:69:154:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:longer distances.
4:131:9553:17:17:86:556:121:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We then use US Census Bureau data on spatial concentration patterns throughout all sectors
4:132:9643:17:17:69:557:104:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the economy. We show that industries with concentrated labor requirements, for whom the
4:133:9733:17:18:69:557:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:beneÖts of labor pooling are very strong, also exhibit smaller and denser clusters relative to
4:134:9827:18:0:82:483:69:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:1See also the Arzaghi and Henderson (2008) mapping of advertising agencies in Manhattan.
5:135:9916:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:industries without this need. A comparison of di§erences between agglomeration due to Mar-
5:136:10006:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:shallian forces and those due to natural advantages (e.g., access to waterways) further conform
5:137:10101:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to our modelís predictions. This empirical work primarily employs continuous agglomeration
5:138:10191:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:metrics like that of Duranton and Overman (2005), and we use traits of industries in the United
5:139:10286:17:17:69:522:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Kingdom to conÖrm the causal direction of these relationships (e.g., Ellison et al. 2010).
5:140:10376:17:17:86:556:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our work makes several contributions to the literature on industrial agglomeration. Most
5:141:10464:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:importantly, we provide a theoretical connection between observable cluster shapes and the
5:142:10554:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:underlying agglomerative forces that cause them. At the core of this contribution is the simple
5:143:10649:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mechanism of including interaction costs among Örms.  The resulting framework provides a
5:144:10737:17:17:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:theoretical foundation for inferring properties of agglomerative forces through observed spatial
5:145:10833:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentrations of industries. We identify settings in which such inference is appropriate, as well
5:146:10931:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as key properties of agglomeration in such settings. An additional contribution of our work,
5:147:11023:17:17:69:557:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:discussed in greater detail later, is to provide a micro-foundation for using continuous spatial
5:148:11119:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:density measurements that center on bilateral distances between Örms. This class of metrics
5:149:11210:17:17:69:387:461:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:includes the popular Duranton and Overman (2005) metric.2;3
5:150:11269:17:17:86:556:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our central empirical contribution is a framework, motivated by our theoretical model, for
5:151:11359:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:meaningful analysis of agglomerative forces with continuous distance horizons. Previous work
5:152:11451:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:considers how agglomerative forces a§ect spatial concentration over di§erent distance horizons,
5:153:11546:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for example up to 75 or 250 miles (e.g., Rosenthal and Strange 2001, 2004; Duranton and
5:154:11633:17:17:69:557:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Overman 2005, 2008; Ellison et al. 2010). Our framework is an important step towards jointly
5:155:11725:17:17:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:considering agglomeration at di§erent distances (25, 75, and 250 miles) simultaneously. This
5:156:11817:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:paper provides a Örst rationale for this type of analysis, and we hope that future research can
5:157:11912:17:17:69:418:325:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:similarly analyze other factors that govern cluster shapes and sizes.4
5:158:11982:17:17:86:556:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Section 2 presents our theoretical model and connects it to empirical measurement of ag-
5:159:12070:17:17:69:557:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:glomeration. Section 3 tests the model using variations across patent citation clusters. Section 4
5:160:12168:17:17:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:presents the second empirical analysis that uses variations in industrial agglomeration for many
5:161:12264:17:18:69:330:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sectors of the economy. The last section concludes.
5:162:12315:18:14:82:557:239:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:2Studies of agglomeration metrics include Ellison and Glaeser (1997), Maurel and SÈdillot (1999), Marcon and

5:166:12752:10:7:69:335:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ally equivalent in prior work (e.g., Ellison and Glaeser 1997).
5:167:12815:7:15:82:557:187:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:4Related studies include Rosenthal and Strange (2001, 2003, 2004, 2008), Duranton and Overman (2005,
5:168:12915:15:11:69:557:172:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:2008), Ellison and Glaeser (1997, 1999), Audretsch and Feldman (1996), Head and Mayer (2004), Arzaghi and
5:169:13020:11:11:69:557:161:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Henderson (2008), Ellison et al. (2010), Greenstone et al. (2010), Delgado et al. (2009), Holmes and Lee (2009),
5:170:13132:11:11:69:557:150:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Fallick et al. (2006), Glaeser and Kerr (2009), Menon (2009), Bleakley and Lin (2010), Alcacer and Chung (2007),
5:171:13244:11:11:69:557:139:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Peíer and Vertinsky (2009), Alfaro and Chen (2010), and Dauth (2010). Our work also connects to studies of the
5:172:13354:11:10:69:557:128:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:shapes of cities (e.g., Lucas and Rossi-Hansberg 2002, Baum-Snow 2007, 2010, Glaeser 2008, and Saiz 2010) and

5:175:13685:10:0:69:211:97:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:literature on economic networks.
6:176:13718:0:28:69:295:699:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:2  Theoretical Framework
6:177:13742:28:17:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We now introduce a model of Örm location choice that generates large agglomeration clusters

7:234:17746:24:17:69:557:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:So far, our model has more or less followed a standard structure: proximity to resources and

7:238:18103:17:17:69:556:328:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f22:sites. Firms in industryAmust paycAKto interact with a natural advantage site andcAAto
7:239:18189:17:27:69:278:311:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f22:interact with another Örm in industryA.
7:240:18228:27:17:86:556:284:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These Öxed costscA-relate to the costs of transporting goods, people, or ideas across Örms.

7:244:18598:17:17:69:557:216:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:required for tacit technologies.  It is also easier to transport some natural advantages (e.g.,
7:245:18693:17:17:69:266:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lumber) than others (e.g., waterways).
7:246:18731:17:17:86:556:182:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Firms only invest in establishing contacts when the beneÖts of doing so equal or exceed the
7:247:18822:17:17:69:556:165:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:associated costs of interaction. SpeciÖcally, Örmionly invests in type--contact with sitejif

8:285:20982:28:25:69:296:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.3.1  Basic DeÖnitions and Structure

8:288:21205:17:17:69:557:142:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:its cluster, but all Örms in a cluster are interconnected. Our measure of agglomeration counts
8:289:21299:17:17:69:557:125:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the number of these clusters that are expected to arise for an industry. The use of an expectation
8:290:21397:17:17:69:556:108:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:is necessary because Örms choose randomly when indi§erent between sites. Firms in industryA
8:291:21488:17:18:69:414:91:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:exhibit agglomeration if they typically occupy few distinct clusters.
8:292:21557:18:13:82:557:73:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:6Here, by saying that the maximal radius gets ìsmallerîor ìlarger,îwe refer to the standard vector ordering:

10:344:24850:17:17:86:556:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The sequential Ölling of clusters explains how large-area clustering may arise in an industry

10:348:25207:17:17:86:556:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A consequence of the maximal radius, however, is that clusters can reach their capacity, at
10:349:25298:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which point the next entrant for the industry will locate elsewhere. In Figure 2a, the closest
10:350:25392:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:remaining site to the existing cluster is site X, but this location is beyond the spillover ranges
10:351:25490:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of any of the populated sites in the cluster. As the marginal entrant cannot proÖtably interact
10:352:25585:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with the cluster, it is indi§erent among sites X, Y, Z, and any other unoccupied site. It will
10:353:25679:17:17:69:391:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:choose its location based upon its idiosyncratic preferences-i;j.
10:354:25744:17:17:86:556:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Likewise, when natural advantages are important to industryA, Örms Öll clusters near at-
10:355:25832:17:17:69:557:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:traction sitesK(A)whenever possible. Figure 2b depicts the simple case where an industry does
10:356:25925:17:17:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not have any Marshallian spillovers, but a series of attraction sites are present and important for
10:357:26024:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:location choice. The maximal radius in this Ögure shows the range around each attraction site
10:358:26117:17:17:69:557:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where Örms can proÖtably interact with the attraction site. A boundary or edge of the cluster
10:359:26210:17:17:69:144:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:again emerges.
10:360:26224:17:27:86:516:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The preceding observations suggest a natural notion of agglomeration in our model:
10:361:26306:27:17:69:556:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:DeÖnition 1.Thelevel of agglomeration in industryAfor maximal radius-Ais the expected
10:362:26391:17:27:69:550:247:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of distinct-A-clustersB-A(j)about sitesj2Z[K(A)occupied by industry-AÖrms.
10:363:26472:27:17:86:557:220:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f22:We say that Örms are(weakly) more agglomerated with respect to maximal radius-1than
10:364:26555:17:17:69:557:203:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f4:they are with respect to radius-2if, holdingNAÖxed, fewer clusters of industry-AÖrms form
10:365:26644:17:17:69:557:186:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when the maximal radius is-1than when it is-2. Note that agglomeration increases as the
10:366:26731:17:17:69:557:169:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:expected number of clusters decreases. Holding industry size constant, increased agglomeration
10:367:26825:17:17:69:330:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:therefore also corresponds to increased cluster size.
10:368:26878:17:17:86:556:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our discussion of the marginal entry decision also highlights the core di§erence between
10:369:26966:17:17:69:557:118:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our structure and prior work. Without considering interaction costs, strictly positive spillover
10:370:27062:17:17:69:557:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:beneÖts exist at all distances. Industries may di§er in how fast or slow Marshallian beneÖts decay,
10:371:27161:17:17:69:557:84:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:but these di§erences in Marshallian forces do not impact the number of clusters. Regardless of
10:372:27255:17:0:69:557:67:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whether the potential spillover beneÖt is large or miniscule, marginal entrants always select sites
11:373:27355:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:closest to the developing cluster regardless of distance (i.e., site X next in Figure 2a). As a
11:374:27450:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consequence, one cluster always forms for an industry, and entrants select sites in an exact order
11:375:27548:17:17:69:155:665:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:in all industries.8
11:376:27567:17:17:86:556:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Thus, the simplest framework does not provide a foundation for relating di§erences in spatial
11:377:27660:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentration for industries to their underlying agglomerative forces. Yet, our intuitive addi-
11:378:27755:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tion of interaction costs provides additional traction by establishing a spatial range over which
11:379:27852:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:interactions are relevant. This localization in turn provides meaningful di§erences in cluster
11:380:27946:17:28:69:348:580:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:formation. We now turn to these comparative statics.9
11:381:27999:28:25:69:385:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.3.2  Agglomeration due to Marshallian Advantages
11:382:28049:25:17:69:557:527:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 2a illustrates the consequences of a longer maximal radius for cluster formation. We
11:383:28140:17:17:69:557:510:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:enlarge the e§ective spillover range for site B to the wider circle. While we only enlarge site Bís
11:384:28239:17:17:69:557:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:circle for visual clarity, the comparative static we have in mind is one in which all Örms in the
11:385:28336:17:17:69:557:476:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:industry have a longer spillover range equivalent to site Bís. Under the larger maximal radius,
11:386:28431:17:17:69:557:459:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the marginal entrant is no longer indi§erent over sites, but would instead choose site X. Thus,
11:387:28526:17:17:69:557:442:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a longer maximal radius is (weakly) associated with greater industry agglomeration as fewer
11:388:28617:17:17:69:215:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters form in expectation.
11:389:28646:17:17:86:556:408:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f7:More formally, recall that-AAis the maximal radius for intra-industry spillovers,-AA-maxfd:
11:390:28737:17:17:69:556:391:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:GAA(d)-cAAg:SinceZ[K(A)is Önite, su¢ ciently small changes do not a§ect location choices.
11:391:28826:17:17:69:557:374:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Larger increases in-AA, either due to weaker attenuation in spillover beneÖts or lower interaction
11:392:28924:17:17:69:557:357:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:costs, can lead Örms to organize into fewer clusters. In fact, we may sign this change: so long
11:393:29019:17:17:69:557:340:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as Marshallian forces are su¢ ciently strong, industry-AÖrms become more agglomerated when
11:394:29109:17:17:69:559:323:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:-AAincreases. To simplify our demonstration of this fact in the next proposition, we ìturn o§î
11:395:29203:17:27:69:396:306:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:natural advantage e§ects by temporarily assumingGAK(0) = 0.10
11:396:29264:27:17:69:555:279:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f15:Proposition 2.IfGAK(0) = 0, then a longer maximal radius for intra-industry spillovers-AA
11:397:29353:17:27:69:412:262:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f22:leads to a (weak) increase in the agglomeration level of industryA.
11:398:29420:27:17:86:556:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The idea behind the proof of Proposition 2 is intuitive. A Örmithat is indi§erent across sites
11:399:29514:17:17:69:557:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:chooses its locationj(i)2Zrandomly. But until the sites in clusterB-AA(j(i))are Ölled, they are
11:400:29609:17:17:69:557:201:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more attractive to industry-AÖrms than are unÖlled sites outside ofB-AA(j(i)). If-AAgrows to
11:401:29701:17:21:69:556:184:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f4:^-AA, a radius large enough thatB^-AA(j) =B-AA(j)[B-AA(j0)for somej;j02Z, then the expected
11:402:29792:21:15:82:556:163:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:8This is equivalent to-A!1in our model. Once a Örst entrant for an industry picks a location, the set of
11:403:29896:15:7:69:485:148:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:sites Ölled by the remainingNA-1Örms (whereNA-jfi:A(i) =Agj) is exactly determined.
11:404:29979:7:13:82:557:141:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:9Our discussion and proofs focus on the simple case where spillover beneÖts do not transfer through the
11:405:30082:13:10:69:557:128:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:cluster. Interaction costs are incurred on a bilateral basis, and Örms at the periphery of a cluster only receive
11:406:30195:10:11:69:557:118:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:beneÖts from their immediate neighbors. More generally, our predictions hold for any transmission structures of
11:407:30306:11:11:69:304:107:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:beneÖts through the cluster so long as-AAis constant.
11:408:30359:11:10:79:557:96:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:The theoretical appendix discusses other extensions and attributes of this framework. Most notably, we outline
11:409:30469:10:7:69:246:86:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:some basic spatial dynamics for clusters.
11:410:30510:7:15:78:557:79:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:10The conclusion of Proposition 2 holds whenever natural advantage beneÖts are su¢ ciently small. However,
11:411:30616:15:0:69:451:64:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the assumption thatGAK(0) = 0substantially simpliÖes the demonstration of the result.
12:412:30702:0:17:69:556:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of clusters occupied by industry-AÖrms shrinks. Indeed, whenever a Örm locates in
12:413:30790:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:eitherB-AA(j)orB-AA(j0), industry-AÖrms Öll all ofB^-AA(j)before locating in or starting another
12:414:30886:17:17:69:106:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cluster.
12:415:30894:17:17:86:556:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Three empirical implications of the proof of Proposition 2 are evident in Figure 2a. First,
12:416:30985:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:industries with a longer maximal radius have larger clusters in the sense of having more Örms and
12:417:31082:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:covering a greater spatial area. Intuitively, a longer spillover radius makes sites at the edges of
12:418:31181:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters attractive that are not attractive with a shorter radius. This induces marginal entrants
12:419:31278:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:into choosing these sites rather than starting new clusters. A longer radius can be due to weaker
12:420:31375:17:17:69:336:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:decay of spillover beneÖts or lower interaction costs.
12:421:31429:17:17:86:556:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The second and third predictions are closely related. A longer spillover radius yields fewer
12:422:31521:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters for a given industry size. As clusters grow in size, fewer clusters are needed to house the
12:423:31621:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:NAÖrms in the industry. Finally, clusters are less dense. The longer radius activates sites at
12:424:31715:17:17:69:557:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the edges of a cluster that are too spatially distant to proÖtably interact with previous entrants
12:425:31813:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:if the radius is shorter. Thus, growth in cluster size is simultaneous with reduction in cluster
12:426:31909:17:17:69:108:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:density.
12:427:31917:17:17:86:556:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our result that clusters due to a longer maximal radius are less dense is the same as saying
12:428:32009:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that average bilateral distances among Örms within the clusters increase. The modelís structure,
12:429:32105:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:however, contains a much more powerful implication regarding spillover lengths and the complete
12:430:32200:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distribution of bilateral distances within clusters. We draw out this implication in Section 2.4.3
12:431:32298:17:28:69:355:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:after introducing empirical measurement more formally.
12:432:32352:28:25:69:361:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.3.3  Agglomeration due to Natural Advantages

13:452:33944:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:result holds. Figure 2b illustrates this case, and the same empirical predictions regarding the

13:455:34144:30:25:69:402:533:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.4  Empirical Measurement of Agglomeration
13:456:34187:25:17:69:557:508:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:As a Önal step, we connect our theoretical framework to empirical metrics of agglomeration

13:461:34631:17:17:86:556:423:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Establishing this connection also has the nice corollary of showing how our model micro-
13:462:34719:17:29:69:555:406:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:founds the use of continuous agglomeration metrics like that of Duranton and Overman (2005).11

13:489:36015:16:14:78:557:83:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:11Historically, continuous agglomeration metrics have generally been designed to meet a set of speciÖed criteria

14:493:36372:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:density functions are calculated separately for each technology or industry analyzed. Industries
14:494:36468:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where establishments tend to pack together tightly in cities, for example, are measured to have

14:496:36610:17:17:86:556:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:While the density function is of direct interest, it is also important to compare the observed

14:527:38369:28:25:69:411:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.4.2  Ordering and Characterizing Agglomerative Forces
14:528:38424:25:17:69:557:145:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Having introduced the DO metric, we now connect our modelís focus on spillover lengths and
14:529:38514:17:17:69:557:128:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cluster shapes to this empirical measurement. Before proceeding, however, it is helpful to recall
14:530:38611:17:18:69:557:111:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that the structure required for Propositions 2 and 3 is minimal. These propositions build directly
14:531:38709:18:13:78:557:93:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:12The empirical appendix further discusses the summation of localized agglomeration levels into aggregate
14:532:38814:13:10:69:557:80:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:statistics similar to DOís global indices. Our technique does not require this step, as we instead interpret local
14:533:38928:10:9:69:557:70:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:deviations directly (although one can use global metrics and their gradients as well). We thank Gilles Duranton
14:534:39039:9:0:69:219:61:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for pointing this feature out to us.
15:535:39077:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on the agglomeration cluster theory to demonstrate that adjustments of the unobserved maximal
15:536:39170:17:17:69:362:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:radius a§ect cluster shapes and sizes in predictable ways.
15:537:39228:17:17:86:556:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The theory speciÖcally suggests that longer maximal spillover radii are associated with fewer,
15:538:39322:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:larger, and less-dense clusters. It is feasible to use these observed traits in di§erent industries

15:541:39611:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:technologies against a measure of the density of technology clusters over 50 miles. These tests,

15:543:39802:17:17:69:551:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:also do not provide a comparison to expected behavior similar to the DO conÖdence intervals.
15:544:39894:17:17:86:556:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:With additional structure, we can jointly quantify these predictions within the DO frame-
15:545:39983:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:work. It is impossible to measure directly theGA-functions that determine the value of Örm
15:546:40073:17:17:69:556:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clustering. However, observed spatial location patterns within industryAallow us to model
15:547:40162:17:17:69:556:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the behavior of the unobserved functionsGA-via an observation that is immediate from the

15:549:40277:27:17:69:556:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f22:Proposition 4.HoldingGAK(GAA) and-AÖxed, and assuming that theGA-are di§erentiable
15:550:40359:17:17:69:556:434:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f22:functions, an increase in the magnitudej(GAA)0j(j(GAK)0j) of the derivative(GAA)0((GAK)0) leads

15:561:41327:17:17:69:557:237:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:maximal radius a§ects the shapes of clusters. The predictions that clusters become larger and
15:562:41420:17:17:69:557:220:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:less dense become jointly visible. Moreover, we can observe the ináuence using regular step sizes
15:563:41517:17:17:69:128:203:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in distance.
15:564:41529:17:17:86:556:186:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:LetSdenote the set of sites occupied by Örms in equilibrium, with many industries present in
15:565:41621:17:17:69:557:169:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the economy. The null hypothesis is that neither agglomeration nor dispersion occurs in industry
15:566:41717:17:17:69:556:152:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:Aat a given bilateral distancedwhen the maximal radius is-A. This hypothesis is equivalent to

15:570:42022:17:17:86:556:84:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:We empirically proxy the set of potential sitesZwith the observed set of actual sitesS
15:571:42108:17:0:69:557:67:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for all businesses. With this assumption, the DO density measures can quantify localization by
16:572:42204:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:comparing observed localization levels to counterfactuals representing the underlying distribution
16:573:42302:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of economic activity typical for a bilateral distance. The null hypothesis is rejected if the localized
16:574:42405:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:density of Örms in industryAis a substantial departure from counterfactuals having the same

16:576:42559:27:25:69:438:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.4.3  Bilateral Distance Gradients in Agglomeration Clusters
16:577:42620:25:17:69:557:596:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:There is an additional beneÖt to connecting our model to these continuous structures. We earlier
16:578:42716:17:17:69:557:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:noted that our empirical implication of smaller, denser clusters for a shorter maximal radius is
16:579:42812:17:17:69:557:562:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equivalent to saying that the mean bilateral density for clusters declines. The model, however,
16:580:42907:17:17:69:557:545:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:has a much stronger implication for how spillover length ináuences the distribution of bilateral
16:581:43003:17:25:69:197:528:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distances within clusters.
16:582:43029:25:17:69:557:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f6:Proposition 5.There is some-- >(d;d)so that whenever-and-0are such that(d;d)< - <
16:583:43110:17:17:69:556:486:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f22:-0<--, then the mean intra-cluster Örm distance is (weakly) smaller when the maximal radius is
16:584:43204:17:25:69:172:469:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f22:-than when it is-0.
16:585:43223:25:17:86:556:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This result describes a key comparative static across spillover lengths.  When comparing
16:586:43311:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:two industries, we earlier established that the industry with the shorter maximal radius should
16:587:43406:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:exhibit denser clusters such that very close bilateral distances are common. This proposition
16:588:43499:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:further identiÖes that this greater representation should be at its highest at the shortest bilateral
16:589:43600:17:17:69:557:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distances possible (i.e., among locations that are located very near to each other). This higher
16:590:43696:17:17:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:frequency should then (weakly) decline as one considers bilateral distances further from the
16:591:43788:17:17:69:228:342:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:shortest possible connections.14
16:592:43820:17:17:86:556:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To provide intuition, Örst consider the impact of the marginal entrant on the bilateral dis-
16:593:43912:17:17:69:557:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tances in Figure 2a. As site X becomes part of the cluster, the kernel density (4) incorporates
16:594:44007:17:17:69:557:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the bilateral distance from site X to every other populated site in the cluster into the spatial
16:595:44103:17:17:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:description. Some of the added bilateral distances are shorter than those that already existed in
16:596:44200:17:17:69:557:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the cluster, with the distance between sites X and B, for example, being less than the distance
16:597:44295:17:17:69:557:240:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between sites B and C. Yet, all of the additional bilateral distances are longer than the closest
16:598:44392:17:17:69:557:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:connections possible (e.g., those surrounding site C). Thus, as the cluster expands and becomes
16:599:44487:17:17:69:557:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:less dense, the relative impact on densities is highest at the shortest possible connections and
16:600:44583:17:17:69:307:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:proceeds (weakly) outwards for some distance.
16:601:44628:17:17:86:556:172:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:An empirical example can also help. Assume that the premium for proximity is higher for
16:602:44715:17:17:69:557:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:investment bankers than it is for accountants. We predict that clusters of investment bankers
16:603:44808:17:17:69:557:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:should exhibit shorter mean bilateral distances among Örms than clusters of accountants do.
16:604:44899:17:18:69:557:121:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:When comparing the spatial distributions of their clusters, Proposition 5 further indicates that
16:605:44995:18:13:78:557:103:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:13As discussed in the empirical appendix and Barlet et al. (2009), this approach is slightly strained for the
16:606:45104:13:7:69:354:90:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:largest industries but is a reasonable baseline for most industries.
16:607:45172:7:14:78:557:83:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:14The conditions of Proposition 5 indicate that this e§ect may disappear when the maximal radius is very
16:608:45276:14:9:69:557:69:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:large. This is a natural consequence of approaching a limit where the maximal radius is so long as to no longer
16:609:45387:9:0:69:188:60:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ináuence cluster formation.
17:610:45416:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the greater density for investment banking should be at its highest at the spatial level of being
17:611:45513:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in the same building or on the same block. When looking at Örms being Öve blocks away from
17:612:45603:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:each other, the spatial density for investment bankers can still exceed that of accountants, but
17:613:45699:17:17:69:543:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the di§erence should not be higher than it is when looking at being next door to each other.
17:614:45791:17:17:86:556:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This requirement micro-founds use of continuous density metrics like (4) to assess whether
17:615:45881:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:di§erences in agglomerative forces across industries yield meaningful deviations in agglomeration
17:616:45978:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:behavior. To summarize, we should empirically see that the greater density associated with a
17:617:46070:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:shorter maximal radius is at its maximum at the closest possible distance on the spatial scale
17:618:46164:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(the intercept of DO) and (weakly) decline thereafter for some distance. Eventually, a distance
17:619:46259:17:17:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is reached where the bilateral densities are the same even with the di§erences in maximal radius.
17:620:46356:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Continuing with our earlier example, the o¢ ces of investment bankers and accountants may be
17:621:46448:17:17:69:441:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equally represented when looking at Örms that are ten city blocks apart.
17:622:46520:17:17:86:556:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:After this point, a distance interval follows with relative under-representation for the cluster
17:623:46616:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:associated with the shorter maximal radius. Finally, once spatial distances are reached that rep-
17:624:46713:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:resent distances between agglomeration clusters for Marshallian industries, the relative densities
17:625:46811:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:again converge. In our example, accounting Örms should be more represented than investment
17:626:46901:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:bankers when looking at businesses 15-20 blocks from each other. This higher representation
17:627:46992:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of accountants should then decline as we consider progressively longer distances that start to
17:628:47086:17:17:69:196:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:exceed the sizes of cities.
17:629:47113:17:17:86:556:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:By contrast, our model generally does not make predictions for bilateral distances across
17:630:47202:17:17:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Marshallian industries beyond the spatial horizons of individual clusters. The behavior of longer
17:631:47299:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:horizons depends upon the underlying distribution of cluster sites and it is thus ambiguous in
17:632:47393:17:17:69:557:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our general framework. The median bilateral distance for all Örms within an industry, for exam-
17:633:47488:17:17:69:557:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ple, can increase or decrease with a longer maximal radius depending upon the spatial distances
17:634:47583:17:17:69:557:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:among the multiple, growing agglomeration clusters and the newly activated sites surround-
17:635:47673:17:17:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing them. Our predictions at this scale instead relate to the distinctions between Marshallian
17:636:47767:17:28:69:243:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spillovers and natural advantages.
17:637:47801:28:25:69:505:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.4.4  Distinguishing between Marshallian and Natural Advantage Forces
17:638:47871:25:17:69:557:204:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Finally, we determine conditions under which we can empirically separate agglomeration due to
17:639:47964:17:17:69:557:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Marshallian spillovers from that due to natural advantages. We generally do not observe the
17:640:48055:17:17:69:557:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:locations of natural attraction sites, hence it is not possible to distinguish these forces in every
17:641:48155:17:17:69:557:153:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:setting. Put another way, there is always some inherent limit to our observational capacity:
17:642:48247:17:17:69:557:136:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we may not be able to determine whether Örms are clustering around an unobserved natural
17:643:48335:17:17:69:202:119:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:advantage or each other.15
17:644:48361:17:18:86:556:102:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Analogous results have arisen in the work of Ellison and Glaeser (1997, 1999), DO, and
17:645:48447:18:13:78:557:84:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:15It may be possible to elucidate this with a dynamic approach; some intuitions along these lines are given in
17:646:48557:13:0:69:178:71:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the theoretical appendix.
18:647:48584:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:others. Historically, this feature of agglomeration measurement has been viewed as an advantage,
18:648:48680:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rather than a deÖciency, since it means that localization levels are determined in a fashion
18:649:48772:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unencumbered by distinctions between sources of agglomerative forces.  The solution to the
18:650:48862:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Ellison and Glaeser (1997) location choice model, which is the micro-foundation of their widely
18:651:48957:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:used metric, is the same in both scenarios. However, this indeterminacy is not desirable when
18:652:49050:17:17:69:549:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:analyzing and contrasting the determinants of agglomeration (e.g., Ellison and Glaeser 1999).
18:653:49143:17:17:86:556:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Unlike in previous work, our framework allows us to partially infer the trade-o§ between
18:654:49231:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Marshallian forces and natural advantage dependency when attraction sites are su¢ ciently far
18:655:49324:17:27:69:100:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:apart.
18:656:49330:27:17:69:556:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f22:Proposition 6.Suppose thatNAis su¢ ciently small. Then, there is a constant-such that if
18:657:49418:17:17:69:557:519:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f22:the minimal distance between attraction sites forAis bounded below by-, and-AKandGAKare
18:658:49505:17:27:69:476:502:12:g_d0_f22:12:g_d0_f22:held Öxed, scalingGAAby a constant- >1will (weakly) increase agglomeration.
18:659:49580:27:17:86:556:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Proposition 6 indicates that when natural advantages are su¢ ciently far away from each
18:660:49667:17:17:69:557:458:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:other, dense agglomeration in small industries is likely driven by Marshallian factors, while
18:661:49760:17:17:69:557:441:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:natural advantage dependency is likely to drive agglomeration observed at longer horizons. If
18:662:49853:17:17:69:557:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:coal mines or state colleges have su¢ cient distance between them, and an industryís location
18:663:49946:17:17:69:557:407:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:choices are heavily ináuenced by being near to one of these attraction sites, the cluster sites for
18:664:50045:17:17:69:557:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this industry will generally be more dispersed than industries that are not ináuenced by these
18:665:50139:17:31:69:555:373:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:attraction sites. This observation is empirically conÖrmed below for a set of natural advantages.16
18:666:50238:31:24:69:281:342:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.5  Our Empirical Approach
18:667:50265:24:17:69:557:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our model connects the maximal radius of interaction for an industry with the shape, density,
18:668:50358:17:17:69:557:301:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and number of clusters it forms. We test these predictions empirically in the next two sections.
18:669:50454:17:17:69:418:284:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For clarity, we Örst describe how our empirical analyses Öt together.
18:670:50523:17:17:86:556:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The graphical analysis in Figure 2a highlights that one approach for testing the model would
18:671:50615:17:17:69:557:250:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:be to identify marginal entrants into clusters by industry and infer from their relative spatial
18:672:50711:17:17:69:557:233:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:location the maximal radius. This would be particularly powerful as the technique could be
18:673:50801:17:17:69:557:216:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:applied to any setting. While quite interesting, multiple data constraints, measurement issues,
18:674:50896:17:17:69:557:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and interpretation questions suggest this be left for future research. We thus take two simpler,
18:675:50992:17:17:69:434:182:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more transparent approaches that separately test aspects of the model.
18:676:51062:17:17:86:556:165:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our Örst test, presented in Section 3, uses patent citation data to measure the maximal radii
18:677:51155:17:17:69:557:148:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that exist in di§erent technology Öelds. This work closely links with technology or knowledge
18:678:51248:17:17:69:557:131:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spillovers as a rationale for agglomeration.  Returning to Figure 2a, our strategy is to use
18:679:51340:17:17:69:556:114:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:citation rates across bilateral distanceswithinclusters to determine whether (and how) distant
18:680:51434:17:18:69:556:97:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örms interact. By estimating the relative frequencies of B!A and B!C citations among the
18:681:51522:18:14:78:557:79:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:16It is important to note that, while our general framework can encompass many varieties of natural advantages,
18:682:51633:14:0:69:501:65:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:this prediction focuses on more structured settings with minimum distances across attraction sites.
19:683:51734:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sites in Figure 2a, we can develop a reasonable proxy of the maximal radius.  We can then
19:684:51823:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:investigate whether di§erences in maximal radius by technology produce the predicted variations
19:685:51918:17:17:69:167:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in clustering traits.
19:686:51939:17:17:86:556:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our second test in Section 4 is much broader in scope. We examine di§erences in agglom-
19:687:52026:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:eration across many industries and sectors in the US economy. This broader approach means
19:688:52115:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that we can no longer identify the micro-interactions among Örms. We instead pursue a more
19:689:52205:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:reduced-form approach where we take from the agglomeration literature traits of industries that
19:690:52300:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increase their desire to agglomerate for labor pooling or around natural advantage sites. We
19:691:52392:17:35:69:535:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:show how ordering industries by these traits produces the patterns predicted in our model.
19:692:52482:35:26:69:332:528:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:3  Patent Technology Clusters
19:693:52511:26:25:69:409:502:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.1  Patent Citations and Knowledge Spillovers
19:694:52557:25:17:69:557:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We employ individual records of patents granted by the United States Patent and Trademark
19:695:52646:17:17:69:557:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:O¢ ce (USPTO) from January 1975 to May 2009.  Each patent record provides information
19:696:52731:17:17:69:557:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:about the invention (e.g., technology classiÖcation, Örm or institution) and the inventors sub-
19:697:52826:17:17:69:557:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mitting the application (e.g., name, address). Hall et al. (2001) provide extensive details about
19:698:52923:17:17:69:557:409:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:these data, and Griliches (1990) surveys the use of patents as economic indicators of technology
19:699:53019:17:17:69:557:392:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:advancement. The data are extensive, with over eight million inventors and four million granted
19:700:53114:17:17:69:206:375:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:patents during this period.
19:701:53141:17:17:86:556:358:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A long literature exploits patent citations to measure knowledge di§usion or spillovers. A
19:702:53231:17:17:69:557:341:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of studies examine the importance of local proximity for scientiÖc exchanges, generally
19:703:53325:17:17:69:556:324:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Önding that spatial proximity is an important determinant of knowledge áows.17Additional work
19:704:53418:17:17:69:557:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:links these local exchanges and economic clusters. Carlino et al. (2007) Önd that higher urban
19:705:53512:17:17:69:557:290:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:employment density is correlated with greater patenting per capita within cities. Rosenthal and
19:706:53607:17:17:69:557:273:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Strange (2003) and Ellison et al. (2010) both Önd that intellectual spillovers are strongest at the
19:707:53706:17:17:69:557:256:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:very local levels of proximity. These empirical patterns closely link to ethnographic accounts of
19:708:53803:17:17:69:359:239:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:economic activity within clusters (e.g., Saxenian 1994).18
19:709:53861:17:17:86:556:222:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Patent citations thus o§er us a unique opportunity to quantify di§erences in spillover radii
19:710:53953:17:17:69:557:205:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and cluster shapes.  It is important, however, to recall several boundaries of this approach.
19:711:54046:17:17:69:557:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:First, patent citations can reasonably proxy for technology exchanges, but there are many other
19:712:54141:17:17:69:557:171:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:forms of knowledge spillovers that may behave di§erently (e.g., Glaeser and Kahn 2001, Arzaghi
19:713:54235:17:17:69:557:154:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Henderson 2008).  Second, several studies Önd that patent citations reáect Marshallian
19:714:54325:17:19:69:557:137:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spillovers among Örms other than pure knowledge exchange. Breschi and Lissoni (2009) closely
19:715:54417:19:11:78:557:118:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:17See Ja§e et al. (1993, 2000), Thompson and Fox-Kean (2005), Thompson (2006), and Lychagin et al. (2010).
19:716:54523:11:13:78:557:107:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:18Recent theoretical and empirical work further ties innovation breakthroughs to the clustering of activity
19:717:54630:13:11:69:557:94:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:around the discovery location, suggestive of very short spillover ranges (e.g., Zucker et al.  1996, Duranton
19:718:54739:11:11:69:557:83:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:2007, Kerr 2010). These concepts are central to endogenous growth theory (e.g., Romer 1986), and Desmet and
19:719:54846:11:0:69:406:72:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Rossi-Hansberg (2010) presents a recent model of spatial endogenous growth.
20:720:54923:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:link citations to inventor mobility across neighboring Örms in their sample, and Porter (1990)
20:721:55017:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:emphasizes how technologies embodied in products and machinery can be transferred directly
20:722:55107:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:through customer-supplier exchanges. Our measurements below may encompass these e§ects to
20:723:55196:17:30:69:226:648:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:the extent that they operate.19
20:724:55227:30:25:69:290:618:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.2  Patent Data Construction
20:725:55256:25:17:69:557:593:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Inventors are required to cite the prior work on which their current patent builds. The total
20:726:55349:17:17:69:557:576:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:count of citations made by USPTO domestic and foreign patents granted after 1975 is about 41
20:727:55441:17:17:69:557:559:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:million citations. We Örst restrict this sample to citations where the citing and cited patents
20:728:55536:17:17:69:557:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are both applied for after 1975. This restriction is necessary for collecting inventor addresses.
20:729:55633:17:17:69:557:525:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our second restriction is that both patents have inventors resident in the United States at the
20:730:55728:17:17:69:557:508:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time of the invention with identiÖable cities and zip codes. About 15 million citations remain
20:731:55822:17:17:69:557:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:after these restrictions. Our primary dataset further focuses on the 4.3 million citations that are
20:732:55921:17:17:69:462:474:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:made in a geographical radius of 250 miles or shorter from the citing patent.
20:733:55998:17:17:86:556:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To identify these distances, we employ zip codes from addresses given for inventors. This
20:734:56087:17:17:69:557:440:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dataset combines both zip codes listed directly on patents and representative zip codes taken
20:735:56180:17:17:69:557:423:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from city addresses where zip codes are not listed. Where multiple inventors exist for a patent,
20:736:56276:17:17:69:557:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we take the most frequent zip code; ties are further broken using the order of inventors listed
20:737:56371:17:17:69:557:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on the patent. The spatial radius is deÖned using geographic centroids of zip codes and the
20:738:56462:17:17:69:557:372:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Haversine áat earth formula. We assign a distance of less than one mile to cases where the citing
20:739:56559:17:17:69:290:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and cited patents are in the same zip code.
20:740:56602:17:17:86:556:338:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our analyses below consider how distances between zip codes ináuence patent citation rates.
20:741:56693:17:17:69:557:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Two issues with using inventor zip codes should be noted. A small concern is that our approach
20:742:56787:17:17:69:557:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:does not consider all of the zip codes associated with inventors for some patents, and this may
20:743:56882:17:17:69:557:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lead to mismeasurement in our distance measure over short spatial scales (speciÖcally, an upward
20:744:56978:17:17:69:557:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:bias on the minimum distance). As a check against this concern, we Önd very similar results
20:745:57069:17:17:69:372:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when instead employing only patents with single inventors.
20:746:57127:17:17:86:556:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:More substantively, addresses listed for inventors can be either their home or work address.
20:747:57219:17:17:69:557:219:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:It would be nice to model both distances between work locations and distances between inventor
20:748:57313:17:17:69:557:202:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:home locations. Both of these distances can ináuence technology di§usion, and it is not clear
20:749:57406:17:17:69:557:185:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which is more important. The patent data do not let us separate these two, however, and this
20:750:57498:17:17:69:425:168:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:measurement error biases us against Önding shorter spillover e§ects.20
20:751:57568:17:13:78:557:151:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:19As an additional note, the literature on intellectual spillovers is divided on whether the development of new
20:752:57679:13:10:69:557:138:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:innovations is most aided by having a large concentration of oneís own industry or by industrial diversity. The
20:753:57790:10:9:69:557:128:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:view stressing industrial concentration is most often associated with Marshall, Arrow, and Romer (MAR). The
20:754:57897:9:10:69:557:119:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:MAR model emphasizes the beneÖts of concentrated industrial centers, particularly citing the gains in increasing
20:755:58009:10:9:69:557:109:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:returns and learning-by-doing that occur within industries. The second view, often associated with Jacobs (1970),
20:756:58122:9:10:69:557:100:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:argues that major innovations come when the ideas of one industry are brought into a new industrial sector. This
20:757:58234:10:9:69:557:90:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:perspective stresses that a wealth of industrial diversity is needed to create the cross-fertilization that leads to
20:758:58350:9:10:69:557:81:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:new ideas and entrepreneurial success.  Duranton and Puga (2001) formalize theoretical foundations for this
20:759:58457:10:8:69:379:71:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:model. Our empirical analysis focuses solely on the MAR determinant.
20:760:58525:8:0:78:557:63:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:20While we manually identiÖed work locations for the description of the San Francisco Bay Area in the intro-
21:761:58635:0:24:69:393:699:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.3  Generations of Citations within Clusters
21:762:58680:24:17:69:557:675:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our Örst analysis examines di§erences in spatial scope within clusters for Örst generation citations
21:763:58780:17:17:69:557:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:compared to later generations of citations. This analysis is useful because it provides evidence
21:764:58876:17:17:69:557:641:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for the interconnections among Örms built into our modelís structure. It also introduces the
21:765:58968:17:17:69:507:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:empirical framework that we use to calculate the maximal radius for each technology.
21:766:59052:17:17:86:556:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To introduce the terminology, a Örst generation citation is simply patent A (our focal patent)
21:767:59146:17:17:69:557:590:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:citing patent B. A second generation analysis analyzes the distances from patent A to a patent
21:768:59240:17:17:69:557:573:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C cited by patent B. Third generation citations are similarly calculated through the citations
21:769:59334:17:17:69:555:556:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:made by patent C, and so on.  If spillovers are not fully transmissible through a cluster,21
21:770:59426:17:17:69:557:539:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the maximal radius model predicts that Örst generation citations will be spatially nearer than
21:771:59520:17:17:69:557:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:later generation citations within clusters. This framework thus o§ers evidence about whether
21:772:59612:17:17:69:557:505:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:technology movements through clusters conform to our modelís structure, although other models
21:773:59705:17:17:69:239:488:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:may generate similar predictions.
21:774:59738:17:17:86:556:471:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We undertake this test using patent citations among bilateral pairs of zip codes that are within
21:775:59834:17:17:69:557:454:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:150 miles of each other. To allow for maximum áexibility in the estimations, we construct a
21:776:59925:17:17:69:556:437:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:series of distance rings indexed bydr. Our distance rings start with a ring of one mile or less,
21:777:60021:17:17:69:557:420:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which includes all citations that occur in the same zip code or between close neighbors. The
21:778:60113:17:17:69:557:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:next ring is one mile to Öve miles, and subsequent rings are every Öve miles to 50 miles. Denote
21:779:60209:17:17:69:231:386:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the set of distance rings asDR.
21:780:60240:17:29:86:302:369:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our empirical speciÖcation takes the form
21:781:60281:29:0:111:214:340:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:ln(Citationsz1!z2) =
21:782:60301:0:25:223:240:351:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f13:X
21:783:60302:25:0:218:246:326:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:dr2DR
21:784:60307:0:37:247:556:340:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:\fdr-I(dz1;z2=dr) +\r-ln(Patentsz2) +-z1+"z1!z2;(7)
21:785:60358:37:17:69:556:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:wherez1indexes source zip codes andz2indexes destination zip codes. The regressors of interest
21:786:60452:17:17:69:556:286:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are the indicator variablesI(-)for each distance ring.-z1is a vector of citing zip code Öxed
21:787:60544:17:17:69:556:269:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:e§ects that controls for the overall citation rates by the source zip code.ln(Patentsz2)controls
21:788:60640:17:17:69:557:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for the level of patenting in the destination zip code, which naturally ináuences the likelihood
21:789:60736:17:17:69:557:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of citations occurring. We drop zip codes for which patents and citations are never observed
21:790:60828:17:17:69:557:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:locally. This regression thus describes the deviations in citation rates at di§erent distance bands
21:791:60927:17:22:69:557:201:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from what the spatial distribution of patents would predict. Zip code pairs with distances of 50
21:792:61023:22:9:69:557:179:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:duction, we are unable to replicate this approach for the full patent dataset. This is partly due to time constraints,
21:793:61141:9:10:69:557:170:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:but more importantly it becomes increasingly di¢ cult to assign inventions to facilities in multi-unit Örms. The
21:794:61253:10:10:69:557:160:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:San Francisco Bay Area is a nice case in that single locations typically house both corporate headquarters and
21:795:61363:10:9:69:557:150:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:innovation facilities. This collocation is much less prevalent in the New York City region, for example, where
21:796:61473:9:10:69:557:141:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:major Örms frequently have o¢ ces in Manhattan and in surrounding areas. These multiple o¢ ces even within
21:797:61579:10:9:69:557:131:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:250 mile circles limit the gain from this approach versus simply using known inventor addresses. Aarland et al.
21:798:61690:9:8:69:362:122:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(2007) study the separation of Örm activity into multiple locations.
21:799:61758:8:13:78:556:114:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:21Marshallian spillovers arefully transmissiblethrough a cluster if all sites in a cluster receive identical spillover
21:800:61876:13:10:69:557:101:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:beneÖts from one another, independent of location. In Figure 2a, this would result in Örms at sites A and B
21:801:61983:10:9:69:557:91:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:receiving equal beneÖts from a Örm at site C, even though site C is only within the maximal radius of interaction
21:802:62096:9:10:69:557:82:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of site A. The intuition is that the spillovers of site C are ìtransmittedîto the Örm at site B through the Örm at
21:803:62210:10:0:69:98:72:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:site A.
22:804:62219:0:17:69:288:699:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:to 150 miles serve as the reference group.22
22:805:62263:17:17:86:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3a plots the\fdrcoe¢ cients. First generation citations are remarkably concentrated at
22:806:62356:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:short distances. There is a particular spike at less than one mile, which includes citations within
22:807:62455:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the same zip code. Over half of this excess e§ect is gone when looking at zip codes one to Öve
22:808:62549:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:miles away, which connects to the very localized networking of Arzaghi and Henderson (2008)
22:809:62640:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and the spillover estimations of Rosenthal and Strange (2003, 2008). The additional decline to
22:810:62734:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:zip codes Öve to ten miles away is very modest, after which a steeper decline ensues. A little
22:811:62828:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more than half of the excess e§ect evident at one to Öve miles is gone once 20-25 miles is reached.
22:812:62927:17:17:69:539:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Coe¢ cients for Örst generation citations are statistically di§erent from zero at all distances.
22:813:63023:17:17:86:556:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3a also graphs the spatial patterns of subsequent generations of patent citations. To
22:814:63115:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:construct these later generations, we randomly select one subsequent citation at each generation
22:815:63211:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:per cited patent.  We require that newly selected citations be within 250 miles of the citing
22:816:63304:17:17:69:557:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:patent to maintain geographic proximity, but not necessarily within 250 miles of the original
22:817:63397:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:citing patent. The speciÖcation (7) is again used to compare rates in local distances to the rates
22:818:63495:17:17:69:214:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that exist over 50-150 miles.
22:819:63524:17:17:86:556:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The results are intuitive and agree with the developed model. Earlier generations, or more
22:820:63614:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:immediate interactions, are signiÖcantly stronger at less than one mile than are later generations.
22:821:63713:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Di§erences at one to Öve miles, however, are much more modest. These relative di§erences slowly
22:822:63808:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:decay from Öve miles onward. At longer distances, the spatial overlaps become very similar across
22:823:63905:17:17:69:130:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:generations.
22:824:63917:17:17:86:556:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To provide a second baseline of comparison, we generate random citation pairs comparable to
22:825:64008:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our observed sample. For every patent cited, we randomly draw a patent with a similar patent
22:826:64100:17:17:69:557:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:class and application year. This method has been used extensively in the literature; we add the
22:827:64195:17:17:69:557:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:innovation that the new counterfactual citation must be within a 250 mile radius of the original
22:828:64291:17:17:69:557:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:citing patent. We do not exclude the original cited patent from the draws, and thus we use the
22:829:64385:17:17:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:original citation if there are no other patents with the same technology and application year
22:830:64478:17:17:69:557:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in the deÖned spatial radius. This approach allows us to focus on local geographic areas and
22:831:64570:17:17:69:526:240:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:provide a rough comparison of underlying patent densities with similar technology traits.
22:832:64659:17:17:86:556:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The random citation counterfactual series is signiÖcantly di§erent from zero at short dis-
22:833:64749:17:17:69:557:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tances. This suggests that Örms with closely related technologies locate near each other even
22:834:64842:17:17:69:557:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:within spatial distances of 150 miles or less. Thus, the citation premiums evident at short dis-
22:835:64938:17:17:69:557:172:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tances combine both a higher likelihood to cite proximate neighbors and a higher likelihood to
22:836:65032:17:17:69:557:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cite generally Örms in closely related technologies. While our basic model is interested in both
22:837:65128:17:17:69:557:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of these mechanisms, we can derive further insights into the structure of interconnections within
22:838:65225:17:18:69:513:121:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters by comparing our citation premiums by generation with these counterfactuals.
22:839:65310:18:13:78:557:103:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:22The total sample count for these estimations is 429,400 zip code pairs with non-zero citation counts. We Önd
22:840:65420:13:9:69:557:90:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:very similar results when collapsing destination zip codes into consolidated rings around citing zip codes. Our
22:841:65531:9:10:69:557:81:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:core speciÖcation drops zero citation cells due to the log transformation. We Önd similar results when instead
22:842:65641:10:0:69:518:71:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:recoding zero citations to be one citation for cells where patenting exists but a citation does not occur.
23:843:65749:0:17:86:556:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The citation premiums for Örst and second generation citations at distances of one mile
23:844:65836:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:or less are substantially stronger than those of the random counterfactuals. These deviations
23:845:65929:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gradually decay as distances between locations within clusters lengthen, with the initial decay for
23:846:66028:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örst generation interactions again being much more rapid. These results conÖrm that observed
23:847:66120:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:citations are not simply following from underlying spatial distributions of technologies. Moreover,
23:848:66219:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:even against the random baseline, initial interactions among Örms are most important at very
23:849:66311:17:17:69:282:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:localized distances and decline thereafter.
23:850:66354:17:17:86:556:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The contrast with third and fourth generation citations is also very informative. Third gen-
23:851:66446:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:eration citations are identical to the random counterfactual at distances of one mile or less.
23:852:66540:17:17:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:They then achieve relative importance between distances of Öve and 20 miles, before converging
23:853:66634:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:again to the random counterfactuals. Thus, extended chains of citations only mirror localized
23:854:66727:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:technology distributions at very short spatial scales, but the interconnected hops do aid access-
23:855:66824:17:17:69:557:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing technologies that are farther away in the cluster. Finally, fourth generation citations are
23:856:66919:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:under-represented at distances of less than one mile, whereas they mirror the random baseline
23:857:67012:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thereafter. This suggests that more than three interconnections do not provide additional access
23:858:67108:17:17:69:433:444:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:in technology clusters for the Örst 50 miles compared to 50-150 miles.23
23:859:67180:17:17:86:556:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These di§erences across citation generations suggest that knowledge spillovers are not fully
23:860:67272:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:transmissible through a cluster, but instead follow a pattern indicated by the Silicon Valley
23:861:67365:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:example and our modelís structure. In Figure 2a, the chain of interconnected hops B!A!C
23:862:67452:17:17:69:557:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:aids site Bís access to spillovers from sites around site C. Moreover, the extra strength for Örst
23:863:67550:17:17:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:generation citations over very short distances o§ers a path for identifying maximal radii of Örm
23:864:67646:17:31:69:259:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:interactions that we investigate next.
23:865:67684:31:24:69:430:311:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.4  Maximal Radius and Spatial Cluster Patterns
23:866:67732:24:17:69:557:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our theory connects the maximal radius of Örm interactions with cluster structure. We test
23:867:67822:17:18:69:557:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:these predictions by looking at di§erences across patent technologies in their citation behaviors
23:868:67919:18:17:69:557:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:similar to Figure 3a. We analyze 36 technologies using the sub-category level of the USPTO
23:869:68009:17:28:69:508:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:system and Hall et al. (2001). Examples include Semiconductors, Optics, and Resins.
23:870:68092:28:25:69:372:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.4.1  Basic Calculations and Descriptive Evidence
23:871:68142:25:17:69:557:182:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We proxy the maximal radius of interaction for each technology through the citation patterns
23:872:68234:17:17:69:557:165:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:evident among patents within that technology. We again measure how close citing patents are
23:873:68325:17:17:69:557:148:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:within individual clusters. One technology, for example, may show that most of the citations
23:874:68417:17:17:69:557:131:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that exist within local areas occur across Örms with a bilateral distance of ten miles or less.
23:875:68512:17:17:69:557:114:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:On the other hand, a second technologyís local citations could occur more evenly over distances
23:876:68607:17:14:78:557:97:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:23The patterns in Figure 3a allow for citations within Örms so that later generations of citations and the random
23:877:68720:14:9:69:557:83:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:counterfactual are simple to deÖne. Excluding citations within Örms, the citation premium for Örst generation
23:878:68829:9:10:69:557:74:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:citations at one mile or less is 1.8. The subsequent patterns look very similar. We exclude citations within Örms
23:879:68942:10:0:69:221:64:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in all subsequent citation analyses.
24:880:68980:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:0-70 miles. In the context of Figure 3a, this second industry would have a much áatter citation
24:881:69075:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:premium for short distances. While we cannot put an exact distance on each technologyís max-
24:882:69167:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:imal radius, we can use the di§erences across technologies in these observable citation patterns
