24:883:69263:17:17:69:331:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to proxy relative di§erences in their maximal radii.
24:884:69315:17:17:86:556:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Operationally, we estimate for each technology a Örst generation citation regression similar
24:885:69407:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to that undertaken for all citations in Figure 3a. To develop a single measure of short technology
24:886:69505:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:exchanges, however, we only include indicator variables for bilateral distances of [0,10] miles and
24:887:69604:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(10,30] miles. Thus, the reference group is bilateral zip code pairs of distances between 30-150
24:888:69700:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:miles. Our measure of technology spillover horizons is the observed premium over the Örst ten
24:889:69793:17:17:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:miles compared to this reference group. We exclude within-Örm citations from these calculations.
24:890:69889:17:17:86:556:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A shorter maximal radius is associated with a greater citation premium for the Örst ten miles.
24:891:69983:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The average premium is 0.43. Semiconductors has the greatest value of 0.74 followed by Surgery
24:892:70077:17:17:69:551:495:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:& Medical Instruments at 0.53. Values of less than 0.3 are found in Gas and Pipes & Joints.24
24:893:70170:17:17:86:556:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For each technology, we estimate the continuous DO spatial density metric described above.
24:894:70260:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3b provides descriptive evidence on patent cluster shapes. We group our 36 technologies
24:895:70354:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:into three broad buckets based upon the categories of the USPTO system following Hall et al.
24:896:70446:17:17:69:557:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(2001): Chemicals, Pharmaceuticals, and Medical (categories 1 and 3), Computers, Communi-
24:897:70535:17:17:69:557:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cations, Electrical, and Electronics (2 and 4), and Mechanical and Miscellaneous (5 and 6). The
24:898:70630:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:chart simply provides the fraction of technologies considered localized by distance within each
24:899:70725:17:17:69:231:376:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:grouping using the metric (5).25
24:900:70757:17:17:86:556:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Every technology within the Computers/Electronics grouping shows abnormally high spatial
24:901:70845:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentration over the Örst 30 miles. After 35 miles, however, localization within this group
24:902:70938:17:17:69:557:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:decays rapidly and is mostly gone by 70 miles or thereabouts. On the other hand, the Chem-
24:903:71028:17:17:69:557:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:icals/Medical grouping shows abnormally high spatial concentration over 30-60 miles, with a
24:904:71119:17:17:69:557:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:much slower decay rate thereafter. Finally, there are no material variations by distance in the
24:905:71214:17:17:69:461:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of technologies localized for the Mechanical/Miscellaneous grouping.
24:906:71289:17:17:86:556:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These patterns roughly conform with our predictions, as the unweighted average citation
24:907:71376:17:17:69:557:240:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:premium for technologies in Computers/Electronics (0.48) is greater than in Chemicals/Medical
24:908:71469:17:17:69:557:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(0.43) and then Mechanical/Miscellaneous (0.39).  These di§erences indicate that the maxi-
24:909:71559:17:17:69:557:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mal radius for technology spillovers tends to be shortest in Computers/Electronics, followed by
24:910:71654:17:17:69:557:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Chemicals/Medical and Mechanical/Miscellaneous. Greater requirements for very close knowl-
24:911:71744:17:18:69:557:172:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:edge exchange are visibly associated with shorter, denser spatial clusters.  This description,
24:912:71838:18:13:78:557:154:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:24We Önd similar results to those described below when using other techniques to calculate these spillover
24:913:71944:13:9:69:557:141:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:horizons. Perhaps most interestingly, the patterns are the same when estimating the distance interval required
24:914:72054:9:10:69:557:132:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to halve the citation premium evident at one to Öve miles compared to 70-75 miles or 145-150 miles. These half-
24:915:72165:10:9:69:557:122:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:life calculations mirror typical decay function estimations. The reported technique with the localized citation
24:916:72276:9:10:69:557:113:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:premium over 0-10 miles has the advantage of requiring much less data to compute consistently. This e¢ ciency
24:917:72385:10:10:69:557:103:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:becomes critical when we estimate these patterns at the technology level in the United Kingdom, where we have
24:918:72494:10:7:69:350:93:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:only about a tenth of the patents available in the United States.
24:919:72559:7:13:78:557:86:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:25Distances are calculated using zip code centroids. Computational limitations, primarily around constructing
24:920:72668:13:10:69:557:73:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the counterfactuals, require that we calculate these densities using patents from 1990-1999. We calculate very
24:921:72778:10:0:69:432:63:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:similar densities for a few smaller technologies when instead considering 1975-2009.
25:922:72864:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:however, does not take advantage of the heterogeneity within groups or the intensity of agglom-
25:923:72959:17:28:69:236:682:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:eration, to which we turn next.26
25:924:72992:28:25:69:284:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.4.2  Cross-Sectional Density Plots
25:925:73028:25:17:69:557:629:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3c provides a cross-sectional plot of cluster density and our proxy for maximal radius
25:926:73121:17:17:69:557:612:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by technology.  Density is measured by the share of bilateral distances among patents for a
25:927:73212:17:17:69:557:595:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:technology over 0-50 miles divided by the share of 0-150 miles. Shares range from 30% to over
25:928:73305:17:17:69:557:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:80%, with a very high share indicating that patents in the technology are very densely packed
25:929:73398:17:17:69:378:561:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in one cluster and then mostly absent until the next cluster.
25:930:73459:17:17:86:556:544:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:There is a strong upward relationship between greater citation premiums (shorter maximal
25:931:73547:17:17:69:557:527:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:radii) and greater patent density. Recall that citation premiums are calculated controlling for
25:932:73642:17:17:69:557:510:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the underlying spatial patent distribution, so this relationship is not mechanical. The slope of
25:933:73738:17:17:69:557:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the trend line is 0.875 (0.163). Very clearly, some of the IT industries show exceptional densities.
25:934:73838:17:17:69:501:476:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:The slope of the trend line is 0.336 (0.075) when capping the density ratio at 50%.27
25:935:73923:17:17:86:556:459:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:While this plot suggests a strong correlation between lengths of micro-interactions among
25:936:74012:17:17:69:557:442:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örms and cluster density at the technology level, it is natural to worry about reverse causality.
25:937:74109:17:17:69:557:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Existing cluster shapes and economic geography likely ináuence citation behavior. Moreover,
25:938:74200:17:17:69:557:408:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:technology clusters may have their spatial locations for unmodeled reasons (e.g., historical acci-
25:939:74298:17:17:69:557:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dents, Öxed university locations). The length of patent citations could then be determined by
25:940:74391:17:17:69:293:374:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the geographical features of these locations.
25:941:74436:17:17:86:556:357:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To address this, we calculate similar citation premiums using patent data from the United
25:942:74525:17:17:69:557:340:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Kingdom. Ellison et al. (2010) introduce this technique and discuss its strengths and limitations.
25:943:74623:17:17:69:557:323:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We geocode all city names and postal codes associated with UK inventors. We also manually
25:944:74712:17:17:69:557:306:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:search for addresses of Örms in the United Kingdom with more than Öfty USPTO patents
25:945:74796:17:17:69:557:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to provide more accurate city assignments. Calculating bilateral distances among pairwise city
25:946:74890:17:17:69:557:272:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:combinations, we then estimate a second set of technology-level citation regressions that parallels
25:947:74989:17:17:69:170:255:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our US estimations.
25:948:75008:17:17:86:556:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The UK calculations face several important limitations relative to the US calculations. First,
25:949:75102:17:17:69:557:221:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and most important, there are signiÖcantly fewer data points to estimate these citation premiums
25:950:75198:17:17:69:557:204:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(the UK sample is less than a tenth of the US sample size). Second, the geocoding has greater
25:951:75291:17:17:69:557:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measurement error, perhaps most centrally dealing with London. Finally, there is some selection
25:952:75386:17:18:69:557:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:bias in the set of UK inventors applying for US patent protection.  While these limitations
25:953:75477:18:13:78:557:152:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:26At Örst it may appear odd that a majority of technologies are deemed localized when the conÖdence bands
25:954:75582:13:9:69:557:139:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are selected such that only 5% of the counterfactuals reach them. This is to be expected if agglomerative forces
25:955:75694:9:10:69:557:130:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:exist, however, as the counterfactuals build upon all patent locations. The counterfactuals are not selected such
25:956:75807:10:9:69:557:120:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:that only 5% of technologies will be deemed agglomerated. This levels e§ect for localization, along with its overall
25:957:75923:9:10:69:557:111:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:decline with distance, is predicted by our model if sites are distributed uniformly but agglomerative forces exist
25:958:76037:10:8:69:486:101:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in nearly all technologies. The same pattern is shown in the industrial data in the next section.
25:959:76134:8:13:78:557:93:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:27Five technology sub-categories are residual groups (e.g., Miscellaneous Drugs) where consistent clustering
25:960:76242:13:9:69:557:80:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:concepts may not apply. Our results generally strengthen when excluding these groups, but we keep them in the
25:961:76351:9:0:69:145:71:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:presented results.
26:962:76371:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:restrict our analysis somewhat, the UK results in this section and the next provide important
26:963:76464:17:17:69:551:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:conÖrmation of our modelís predictions in a manner that addresses reverse causality concerns.
26:964:76557:17:17:86:556:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3d provides a cross-sectional plot of US cluster density against UK citation premiums.
26:965:76650:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The vertical axis is the same as Figure 3c, but we substitute the UK citation premiums for
26:966:76740:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the horizontal axis.  Interestingly, the UK citation premiums are weaker than in the United
26:967:76831:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:States on average (mean of 0.24 versus 0.43). This decline may reáect measurement error in
26:968:76921:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distances or more interesting economic di§erences. We do not further investigate, however, as
26:969:77014:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we are primarily interested in relative di§erences across technologies as a proxy for di§erences
26:970:77110:17:17:69:157:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in maximal radii.
26:971:77127:17:17:86:556:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:There are some substantial changes among some IT industries in Figure 3d compared to
26:972:77211:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3c. Most noticeably, semiconductors declines substantially (i.e., its maximal radius is
26:973:77305:17:17:69:557:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not as short as we measure in the US data). Nevertheless, the positive relationship persists
26:974:77397:17:17:69:557:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with cluster density in the United States. A greater citation premium for a technology in the
26:975:77490:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:United Kingdom, corresponding to a shorter maximal radius, links to a denser cluster in the
26:976:77581:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:United States. The slope of the trend line is 0.230 (0.075). The slope of the trend line is 0.159
26:977:77678:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(0.031) when capping the US density ratio at 50%. These patterns provide conÖdence that these
26:978:77771:17:28:69:416:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relationships are not being solely determined by unmodeled factors.
26:979:77838:28:25:69:251:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.4.3  Complete Density Plots
26:980:77867:25:17:69:557:374:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:While transparent, the cross-sectional plots are incomplete in that they do not describe the full
26:981:77964:17:17:69:557:357:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distribution of location behavior. They also do not account for di§erences in industry size, which
26:982:78062:17:17:69:557:340:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:can have a mechanical e§ect on density estimates. We now use the DO methodology to describe
26:983:78153:17:17:69:232:323:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:these patterns more completely.
26:984:78184:17:17:86:557:306:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We begin with the kernel density^KA(d)deÖned in (4) for a technologyA. The process of
26:985:78269:17:17:69:557:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assigning localization (5) involves non-monotonic transformations of the data, and it is thus
26:986:78362:17:17:69:556:272:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:useful to view the simpler density functions Örst. With some abuse of notation, we deÖne^KA;d
26:987:78455:17:17:69:557:255:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as the sum of the kernel density over Öve mile increments starting from zero to Öve miles and
26:988:78548:17:17:69:556:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:extending to 245-250 miles. We again index distance rings withdrand denote the set of distance
26:989:78642:17:17:69:486:221:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rings asDR, although the distance rings are di§erent from the citations analysis.
26:990:78723:17:26:86:486:204:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figures 3e and 3f present coe¢ cients from empirical speciÖcations of the form
26:991:78801:26:0:160:193:178:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:^KA;d=
26:992:78807:0:26:202:219:187:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f13:X
26:993:78808:26:0:196:224:161:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:dr2DR
26:994:78813:0:37:226:556:175:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:\fdr-I(d=dr)-SpilloverDensityA+-d+"A;d:(8)
26:995:78855:37:17:69:557:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These estimations provide a continuous description of how technology cluster shapes vary with
26:996:78948:17:17:69:556:121:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:technology horizons.SpilloverDensityAis the technology spillover density for industryAcal-
26:997:79038:17:17:69:557:104:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:culated through patent citations (i.e., the same as the horizontal axis values in Figures 3c and
26:998:79134:17:17:69:557:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:3d). Greater values ofSpilloverDensityAcorrespond to a shorter maximal radius-Ain our
26:999:79219:17:59:69:557:70:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model, and we thus anticipate Önding denser and smaller clusters for these technologies. We
27:1000:0:59:0:0:12:11:69:699:69:699:0
27:1001:79312:0:21:126:557:703:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f4:^KA;dandSpilloverDensityAto have unit standard deviation to aid interpretation,
27:1002:79391:21:17:69:285:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and we evaluate\fdrat each distance ring.
27:1003:79432:17:17:86:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A vector of distance Öxed e§ects-dcontrols for typical agglomeration densities by distance.
27:1004:79523:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:They thus directly account for the overall spatial density of patenting so that our estimations
27:1005:79618:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consider di§erences across technologies. As the vector of distances fully contains the support of
27:1006:79715:17:17:69:556:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distances, we do not include a main e§ect forSpilloverDensityA. Higher values of\fdrindicate
27:1007:79807:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that technologies with high spillover densities show greater spatial density at that distance. The
27:1008:79905:17:17:69:485:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cross of 51 distances and 36 technologies yields 1836 observations per estimation.
27:1009:79987:17:17:86:556:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figures 3e and 3f present these density estimations using the US and UK measures of
27:1010:80070:17:17:69:556:546:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:SpilloverDensityA, respectively.  Triangles report\fdrcoe¢ cients.  The dashed lines provide
27:1011:80162:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:90% conÖdence bands with standard errors clustered by technology. We Önd similar precision
27:1012:80252:17:17:69:257:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when bootstrapping standard errors.
27:1013:80287:17:17:86:556:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Technologies with greaterSpilloverDensityA, or a shorter maximal radius, are substan-
27:1014:80372:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tially more agglomerated at very short distance horizons.  A standard deviation increase in
27:1015:80463:17:17:69:556:461:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:SpilloverDensityAis associated with a 1.3 standard deviation increase in agglomeration at Öve
27:1016:80556:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:miles using the US measure; the UK-based estimate is 0.6 standard deviations. By 60-75 miles,
27:1017:80649:17:17:69:476:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the abnormal spatial concentration is no longer statistically di§erent from zero.
27:1018:80730:17:17:86:556:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Looking further, technologies with greaterSpilloverDensityAare under-represented after 75
27:1019:80819:17:17:69:557:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:miles or thereabouts. Using the US estimate of citation density, these clusters show an abnormal
27:1020:80915:17:17:69:557:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lack of density from 80 to 185 miles that is statistically di§erent from zero at every Öve mile
27:1021:81010:17:17:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increment. The UK estimation shows a similar pattern, although its point estimates are not
27:1022:81100:17:17:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:statistically di§erent from zero. In both cases, the point estimates converge to zero as distances
27:1023:81198:17:17:69:557:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:approach 250 miles.  At the edge of this spatial scale, di§erences in maximal radius are not
27:1024:81290:17:17:69:404:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:systematically associated with di§erent agglomeration intensities.
27:1025:81356:17:17:86:556:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These patterns closely follow our theory model and the predictions given in Section 2.4.3
27:1026:81445:17:17:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:regarding maximal radii and cluster shapes. Note that the patterns of over-representation fol-
27:1027:81539:17:17:69:557:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lowed by under-representation are not mechanical. Other attributes, for example, could predict
27:1028:81633:17:17:69:493:240:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:higher spatial concentration for a technology at all spatial distances to 250 miles.28
27:1029:81719:17:17:86:556:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figures 3g and 3h take the next step of calculating localized deviations from industry speciÖc
27:1030:81813:17:17:69:557:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:conÖdence intervals using (6). The patterns are very similar to Figures 3e and 3f. The excess
27:1031:81906:17:17:69:557:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:density at very short spatial horizons is robustly di§erent from the random counterfactuals and
27:1032:82001:17:17:69:557:172:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:very similar to the kernel plots. The abnormally low spatial concentration at moderate spatial
27:1033:82095:17:17:69:557:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:horizons is weaker than in the raw kernel density plots, with the US estimator signiÖcantly
27:1034:82186:17:17:69:557:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:di§erent from zero over a narrower range of 120-155 miles. The UK estimator does not show
27:1035:82275:17:17:69:510:121:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:material deviations at moderate horizons once the conÖdence intervals are considered.
27:1036:82360:17:18:86:556:104:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Overall, these Ögures jointly illustrate our central model predictions.  A shorter maximal
27:1037:82450:18:13:78:557:86:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:28The kernel density functions (4) sum to one over the support of all bilateral distances in US, stretching from
27:1038:82562:13:9:69:557:73:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:next door to several thousand miles. This does not materially ináuence the cluster descriptions we develop here
27:1039:82673:9:0:69:171:64:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:over the Örst 250 miles.
28:1040:82699:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:radius, or greater spillover density, is very strongly associated with greater agglomeration at
28:1041:82794:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:very short spatial horizons (i.e., the cluster is denser).  These same technologies tend to be
28:1042:82888:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:under-represented at moderate spatial horizons (i.e., the clusters are smaller). The latter result
28:1043:82986:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is very strong in the raw US data, and it is partially conÖrmed with the UK estimator. Moreover,
28:1044:83082:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in all cases the initial decline in bilateral densities from the closest feasible values that is predicted
28:1045:83188:17:35:69:278:614:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:by Proposition 5 is robustly supported.29
28:1046:83229:35:29:69:498:579:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:4  Marshallian Spillovers and Natural Advantages
28:1047:83277:29:17:69:557:550:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This section uses data from the US Census Bureau to more broadly examine industry agglom-
28:1048:83366:17:17:69:557:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:eration in the United States. We Örst outline the US Census Bureau data employed. We then
28:1049:83455:17:17:69:557:516:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:compute spatial densities using bilateral distances among establishments by industry. We Önally
28:1050:83550:17:17:69:557:499:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:link di§erences in spatial agglomeration patterns to di§erences across industries in Marshallian
28:1051:83646:17:31:69:323:482:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spillovers and dependency on natural advantages.
28:1052:83694:31:25:69:361:451:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4.1  Spatial Densities for Establishments
28:1053:83735:25:17:69:557:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our estimates of industrial agglomeration patterns are developed through conÖdential data
28:1054:83824:17:17:69:557:409:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:housed by the US Census Bureau. The Longitudinal Business Database (LBD) provides an-
28:1055:83909:17:17:69:557:392:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nual observations for every private-sector establishment with payroll from 1976 onward. The
28:1056:84000:17:17:69:557:375:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Census Bureau data are an unparalleled laboratory for studying the industrial structure of US
28:1057:84093:17:17:69:557:358:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örms. Sourced from US tax records and Census Bureau surveys, the micro-records document
28:1058:84180:17:17:69:557:341:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the universe of establishments and Örms rather than a stratiÖed random sample or published
28:1059:84270:17:17:69:557:324:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:aggregate tabulations. In addition, the LBD lists physical locations of establishments rather
28:1060:84363:17:17:69:557:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than locations of incorporation, circumventing issues related to higher legal incorporations in
28:1061:84458:17:17:69:557:290:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:states like Delaware. We deÖne 362 industries through the three-digit level of the 1987 Standard
28:1062:84554:17:17:69:557:273:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Industrial ClassiÖcation (SIC3). Industry assignment is at the establishment level for multi-unit
28:1063:84651:17:17:69:497:256:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örms. The data include 108 million workers and 5.8 million establishments in 1997.
28:1064:84733:17:17:86:556:239:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We use bilateral distances among establishments to create continuous density metrics similar
28:1065:84825:17:17:69:557:222:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to those described for our patent data. Our primary metric weights each establishment equally,
28:1066:84919:17:17:69:557:205:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and we have conÖrmed that an employment-weighted index yields similar results. Localization
28:1067:85010:17:17:69:557:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is typically higher in employment-weighted distributions than in those using plant counts (e.g.,
28:1068:85106:17:17:69:557:171:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Holmes and Stevens 2002).  We measure bilateral distances using distances between county
28:1069:85194:17:18:69:522:154:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:centroids. Establishments in the same county are given a uniform distance of one mile.30
28:1070:85282:18:15:78:557:136:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:29Similar results are found using three additional speciÖcation variants. The Örst employs the density function
28:1071:85393:15:11:69:557:121:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(4) and introduces the conÖdence bandsKLCI-UA(d)andKLCI-LA(d)as precision controls. The second calculates
28:1072:85498:11:10:69:557:110:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a global index similar to DOís main metric and then evaluates the gradient of this concentration measure across
28:1073:85609:10:7:69:471:100:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:distances. Finally, the DO conÖdence bands can be adjusted to a 1%/99% signiÖcance level.
28:1074:85698:7:14:78:557:93:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:30Multiple factors yield conáicting recommendations regarding this latter choiceó for example, accounting for
28:1075:85807:14:9:69:557:79:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:larger land areas versus congestion e§ects with higher urban density. As shown below, the major movements we
28:1076:85915:9:0:69:551:70:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:analyze in this section happen at distances of 50 miles or greater, making this choice of secondary importance.
29:1077:86028:0:17:86:556:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 4a graphs the fraction of industries that are localized at each distance level, akin to
29:1078:86122:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 3b. We analyze 25 mile increments to 1000 miles. Approximately 60% of industries dis-
29:1079:86214:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:play positive localization at each increment to 125 miles. Of the remainder, about 30% display
29:1080:86308:17:17:69:557:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dispersion and 10% show neither pattern. Localization attenuates over moderate distances, and
29:1081:86401:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:only 30% of industries are localized at distances of 900-1000 miles. Manufacturing industries
29:1082:86494:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are more agglomerated at short spatial scales than non-manufacturing industries, a pattern that
29:1083:86589:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:reverses at longer horizons. This result is to be expected, given the transportable and trade-
29:1084:86683:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:able nature of manufactured products. The empirical appendix provides additional descriptive
29:1085:86775:17:31:69:117:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:statistics.
29:1086:86786:31:24:69:258:532:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4.2  Agglomerative Forces
29:1087:86811:24:17:69:557:508:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We develop two traits of industries to model the Marshallian agglomeration and natural advan-
29:1088:86904:17:17:69:557:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tages forces analyzed in our theoretical model. For the former, we focus on labor pooling as a
29:1089:86998:17:17:69:557:474:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rationale for Örm clustering. Multiple models speciÖcally describe the beneÖts of Örm cluster-
29:1090:87092:17:17:69:556:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing due to specialized workforces.31We focus on this feature, recognizing that other forms of
29:1091:87185:17:17:69:505:440:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Marshallian interactions exist (e.g., Rosenthal and Strange 2004, Ellison et al. 2010).
29:1092:87272:17:17:86:556:423:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We measure how concentrated or specialized the occupational needs of an industry are
29:1093:87356:17:17:69:557:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:through the 1999 National Industry-Occupation Employment Matrix (NIOEM) published by
29:1094:87440:17:17:69:557:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the Bureau of Labor Statistics. The NIOEM provides industry-level employments in over 700
29:1095:87529:17:17:69:557:372:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:occupations. We calculate the occupational concentration for each industry as a HerÖndahl-
29:1096:87619:17:17:69:557:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Hirschman Index (HHI) of employments across occupations. Higher values of this index suggest
29:1097:87711:17:17:69:557:338:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:greater concentration of workers in a small number of occupations, which increases the spillover
29:1098:87807:17:17:69:254:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:beneÖts of industrial agglomeration.
29:1099:87843:17:17:86:556:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 4b provides some simple evidence that this labor concentration relates to spatial
29:1100:87931:17:17:69:557:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:scales. We divide industries into terciles based upon their occupational concentration. Highly
29:1101:88025:17:18:69:557:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentrated industries are more likely to be localized at shorter spatial scales; they are less
29:1102:88121:18:17:69:557:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:likely to exhibit localization at longer spatial horizons. Figure 4bís trends are for all industries,
29:1103:88222:17:17:69:431:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and the same patterns hold both within and outside of manufacturing.
29:1104:88290:17:17:86:556:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We next model natural advantages for manufacturing industries using data from the Census
29:1105:88378:17:17:69:557:201:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of Manufacturers.  There are many natural advantages that one could model, and we pick
29:1106:88464:17:17:69:557:184:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Öve for this exercise: coal inputs, natural gas inputs, lumber inputs, agricultural and livestock
29:1107:88561:17:17:69:557:167:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inputs, and dependency upon water transportation. We normalize each of these dependencies
29:1108:88650:17:14:78:557:150:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:31Marshall (1920) described how an agglomeration of workers and Örms shields workers from Örm-speciÖc
29:1109:88751:14:9:69:557:136:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:shocks. Workers can be more productive and better insured by moving from Örms that are hit with negative
29:1110:88855:9:11:69:557:127:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:shocks to better opportunities (e.g., Diamond and Simon 1990, Krugman 1991, Overman and Puga 2010). Larger
29:1111:88961:11:11:69:557:116:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:labor pools further promote more e¢ cient matches (e.g., Helsley and Strange 1990), and multiple Örms protect
29:1112:89070:11:10:69:557:105:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:workers against ex post appropriation of investments in human capital (e.g., Rotemberg and Saloner 2000). All
29:1113:89179:10:9:69:557:95:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:of these mechanisms suggest that Örms that employ similar types of workers will tend to locate near one another
29:1114:89290:9:11:69:557:86:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:and that Örms will beneÖt from thick local markets for their speciÖc labor needs. Glaeser and Kerr (2009) provide
29:1115:89403:11:10:69:557:75:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:a further discussion of this pooling concept. Duranton and Puga (2004) and Glaeser (2008) provide a general
29:1116:89510:10:0:69:300:65:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:theoretical taxonomy of agglomeration determinants.
30:1117:89563:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by industry shipments, and we deÖne a single natural advantages metric for each industry as
30:1118:89654:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:its maximum dependency across these Öve traits. Some of the largest dependencies on natural
30:1119:89745:17:17:69:469:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:advantages are found in food processing, pulp and paper, and steel industries.
30:1120:89823:17:17:86:556:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 4c again provides simple evidence that natural advantages are systematically related
30:1121:89914:17:17:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to spatial scales. We divide manufacturing industries into terciles. In contrast to Figure 4b, the
30:1122:90012:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:most dependent industries on natural advantages are the least likely to be abnormally concen-
30:1123:90105:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:trated at small spatial distances. This dependency instead exhibits itself over horizons of 250 to
30:1124:90203:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:700 miles. The industries most concentrated to 200 miles are those with the least dependency
30:1125:90295:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on natural advantages. The rates of decay at the edges for natural advantages also appear more
30:1126:90389:17:31:69:111:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gradual.
30:1127:90397:31:24:69:414:515:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4.3  Labor Pooling and Spatial Cluster Patterns
30:1128:90444:24:17:69:557:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To more formally test these patterns, we run a series of regressions similar to the patent re-
30:1129:90538:17:17:69:557:474:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gression model (8). We organize the data by industriesAand distancesd. We use 40 distance
30:1130:90627:17:17:69:557:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:intervals, ranging from 0-25 miles to 975-1000 miles, and 353 industries for a total of 14,120
30:1131:90721:17:17:69:557:440:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:observations. We exclude nine industries from our general sample of 362 industries for which we
30:1132:90816:17:17:69:318:423:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cannot calculate all of the explanatory variables.
30:1133:90866:17:17:86:556:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We present the patterns using the basic kernel estimator (4); the results are very similar with
30:1134:90961:17:17:69:557:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the other variants studied in Section 4. We again transform variables to have unit standard de-
30:1135:91056:17:17:69:557:372:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:viation to aid in interpretation. The size variation of these industries is substantially larger than
30:1136:91157:17:17:69:557:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:among patent technologies.32To provide the most representative depictions, we conservatively
30:1137:91249:17:17:69:557:338:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cap extreme densities at their 1% and 99% values by distance and weight by log employment
30:1138:91338:17:17:69:557:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the industry. These speciÖcation steps are not very important, however, and the patterns we
30:1139:91432:17:17:69:341:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:describe are very robust across speciÖcation variants.
30:1140:91486:17:17:86:556:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 4d Örst tests occupational concentration across all industries. Higher occupational
30:1141:91576:17:18:69:557:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentration promotes localization over the Örst 100 miles, with substantial and monotonic
30:1142:91667:18:17:69:557:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:attenuation thereafter. By 250 miles, higher occupational concentration is no longer associated
30:1143:91762:17:17:69:557:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with greater localization at a 90% conÖdence level. The magnitudes are important in economic
30:1144:91854:17:17:69:557:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:size. A standard deviation increase in occupational concentration is associated with a 0.6 stan-
30:1145:91950:17:17:69:557:201:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dard deviation increase in localization to 100 miles. It is also clear that the total length of the
30:1146:92049:17:17:69:557:184:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:agglomeration cluster associated with labor pooling is substantially longer than typical commut-
30:1147:92145:17:17:69:557:167:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing distances (which are frequently less than 40 minutes), akin to the San Francisco example in
30:1148:92240:17:17:69:122:150:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 1b.
30:1149:92250:17:17:86:556:133:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We have conÖrmed this pattern using several other techniques for measuring occupational
30:1150:92337:17:17:69:557:116:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentration or specialization. We Önd similar results when calculating the concentration ratio
30:1151:92433:17:17:69:557:99:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of employment in the most frequent occupations or in the top four occupations. Similarly, we Önd
30:1152:92529:17:14:78:557:82:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:32Counts of patents used in our estimations range from 2811 to over 66,000. Among the industrial data, 18
30:1153:92634:14:0:69:498:68:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:industries have fewer than 100 establishments, while the maximum is over 400,000 establishments.
31:1154:92732:0:17:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the opposite pattern of results when modeling the number of occupations listed. Industries with
31:1155:92827:17:17:69:557:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more listed occupations, regardless of employment levels, are associated with greater dispersion.
31:1156:92924:17:17:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We also Önd that the results are invariant to including other distance-based interactions for
31:1157:93017:17:17:69:502:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:average wage, college share, labor intensity, and the number of Örms in the industry.
31:1158:93102:17:17:86:556:631:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To check that reverse causality is not the case for our labor measures, we calculate the cor-
31:1159:93195:17:17:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:responding occupational concentration of manufacturing industries in the United Kingdom. We
31:1160:93286:17:17:69:557:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:use data from the UK Labour Force Survey, which is similar to the USís Current Population
31:1161:93375:17:17:69:557:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Survey. The patterns in Figure 4e are very similar. This suggests that our results are not due
31:1162:93469:17:17:69:557:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to endogenous selections of production techniques by spatially isolated industries to match local
31:1163:93566:17:17:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:worker environments.33A second advantage of the UK test is that the occupational concentra-
31:1164:93657:17:17:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tions are calculated from a second data source, suggesting that our outcomes are not dependent
31:1165:93751:17:17:69:323:512:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:upon idiosyncratic features of the BLSís NIOEM.
31:1166:93798:17:17:86:556:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The shapes of these distributions mirror Figures 3e-3h. It is important to note, however, the
31:1167:93891:17:17:69:557:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more subtle di§erences in the estimation. A central strength of the patent data is the capacity
31:1168:93986:17:17:69:557:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to model directly the micro-level interactions of Örms to calculate a measure of the maximum
31:1169:94078:17:17:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:radii. While the Census Bureau data allows us to consider many more industries and sectors,
31:1170:94169:17:31:69:513:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this broader dataset requires a reduced-form approach that models traits of industries.
31:1171:94256:31:24:69:455:396:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4.4  Natural Advantages and Spatial Cluster Patterns
31:1172:94308:24:17:69:557:372:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 4f considers natural advantages within the manufacturing sector.  These estimations
31:1173:94398:17:17:69:557:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:control for occupational concentration, with the unreported coe¢ cients being very similar to
31:1174:94491:17:17:69:557:338:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 4d. The contrast between natural advantages and labor agglomeration is very interesting
31:1175:94585:17:17:69:557:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and supports the crossing property of our model described in Proposition 6. High dependency
31:1176:94676:17:17:69:557:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:upon natural advantages is associated with dispersion (a lack of density) at short spatial scales.
31:1177:94774:17:17:69:557:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This follows from coal mines, coastal ports, and similar features naturally having some distance
31:1178:94870:17:18:69:557:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between them. The e§ective radius for transporting goods and material inputs is also longer
31:1179:94961:18:17:69:185:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than for labor pooling.
31:1180:94984:17:17:86:556:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Over the next 500 miles, however, the importance of natural advantages grows. By distances
31:1181:95074:17:17:69:557:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of 400 miles, the agglomerative force of natural advantages exceeds that of labor, and remains
31:1182:95168:17:17:69:557:201:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:strong until about 800 miles. Very clearly, the spatial dimension of natural advantages is longer,
31:1183:95266:17:17:69:557:184:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and it appears that the attenuation rate is weaker, than for the Marshallian agglomeration
31:1184:95356:17:17:69:557:167:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:proxied by our labor features. This is most evident in the modest gradients and long spatial
31:1185:95448:17:17:69:557:150:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:durations of the slope in Figure 4f.  The shapes of these densities conform to our modelís
31:1186:95538:17:17:69:128:133:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:predictions.
31:1187:95550:17:14:78:557:116:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:33Several theoretical models describe spatial location choice and production technology as jointly determined
31:1188:95659:14:0:69:299:102:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:(e.g., Duranton and Puga 2001, Glaeser et al. 2010).
32:1189:95713:0:28:69:191:699:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:5  Conclusion
32:1190:95726:28:17:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This paper introduces a new model of location choice and agglomeration behavior. From a simple
32:1191:95820:17:17:69:557:654:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and general framework, we show that agglomeration clusters generally cover a substantially
32:1192:95910:17:17:69:557:637:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:larger area than the micro-interactions upon which they build. In turn, agglomerative forces
32:1193:96002:17:17:69:557:620:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with longer micro-interactions are associated with fewer, larger, and less-dense clusters. The
32:1194:96096:17:17:69:557:603:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:theory thereby provides a basis for the use of continuous agglomeration metrics that build upon
32:1195:96191:17:17:69:557:586:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:bilateral distances among Örms. The theory also rationalizes the use of observable cluster shapes
32:1196:96288:17:17:69:557:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and sizes to rank order the lengths of underlying agglomerative forces. We Önd conÖrmation of
32:1197:96381:17:17:69:557:552:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our theoretical predictions using both variations across patent technology clusters and variations
32:1198:96479:17:17:69:227:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across industry concentrations.
32:1199:96510:17:17:86:556:518:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We hope that our theoretical framework proves an attractive model for incorporating ad-
32:1200:96597:17:17:69:557:501:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ditional factors that ináuence Örm location and agglomeration behavior. Important extensions
32:1201:96689:17:17:69:557:484:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:include: modelling the dynamics of industry life-cycles, incorporating interactions across Örms in
32:1202:96787:17:17:69:557:467:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:di§erent industries, allowing for pricing of locations, and incorporating the development of new
32:1203:96883:17:17:69:557:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sites. We likewise believe our setting is an attractive laboratory for structural modelling that
32:1204:96979:17:17:69:557:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:would allow recovery of the underlying lengths of micro-interactions. These parameters could
32:1205:97071:17:17:69:557:416:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in turn be useful for understanding spillover transmissions in networks and for studying spatial
32:1206:97167:17:17:69:234:399:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:propagation of economic shocks.
32:1207:97198:17:18:86:556:382:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We have applied our framework to two empirical settings, but we believe that many more
32:1208:97284:18:17:69:557:364:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:applications in industrial agglomeration are possible. For example, future work can look to price
32:1209:97381:17:17:69:557:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters or identify spillover lengths by examining the location decisions of marginal entrants.
32:1210:97477:17:17:69:557:330:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our framework highlights the important information that is contained in these indi§erence
32:1211:97566:17:17:69:557:313:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:conditions if properly identiÖed. As important, we believe our framework describes interactions
32:1212:97661:17:17:69:557:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in many other contexts as well. For example, studies Önd that knowledge áows within Örms
32:1213:97749:17:17:69:557:279:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:or universities are substantially shaped by the physical layout of facilities (e.g., Liu 2010). We
32:1214:97847:17:17:69:557:262:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:hope that future work similarly analyzes parallel situations where costs of interaction generate
32:1215:97943:17:59:69:161:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a maximal radius.

50:2008:137400:17:12:78:421:137:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:41This assumption implicitly deÖnes the constant-of the theorem statement.
50:2009:137474:12:14:78:556:125:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:42We say that both(0;1)2Kand(0;1)2Zas shorthand denoting the fact that there is a site inKand a
50:2010:137569:14:8:69:334:111:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:site inZ, both of which are--close to(0;1)for some small-.
50:2011:137627:8:25:78:180:103:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:43To see this, note that
50:2012:137651:25:0:182:205:78:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f19:(2-+
50:2013:137655:0:9:207:215:87:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:p
50:2014:137656:9:0:216:291:78:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f19:2-1)-((1 +-)(
50:2015:137669:0:9:291:299:87:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:p
50:2016:137670:9:0:299:403:78:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f9:2 +-)-1) =-(1--)-
50:2017:137687:0:9:405:413:87:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:p
50:2018:137688:9:0:413:444:78:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f20:2- >0:
51:2019:137696:0:11:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:complete clusters could be dynamically vacated in favor of more appropriate locations due to
51:2020:137788:11:12:69:193:688:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:entry and exit behavior.
51:2021:137812:12:11:86:556:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:By contrast, when natural advantages dominate Marshallian forces, as under the conditions of
51:2022:137904:11:12:69:557:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Proposition 3, the pattern of location choices for Örms is dynamically stable. If a Örm exits in this
51:2023:138005:12:11:69:556:653:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:scenario, then the newly vacated sitejis the most valuable site available. This is immediate by
51:2024:138100:11:13:69:556:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:virtue of the fact that sitejwas previously selected and all resource attraction sites are known.
51:2025:138197:13:12:69:557:629:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Since natural advantage spillovers dominate, locationjmust be (weakly) optimal relative to
51:2026:138287:12:11:69:556:617:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:other available sites. Thus, if the number of Örms in industryAis constant, then the pattern of
51:2027:138382:11:12:69:446:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Örm locations is constant if natural advantages are of central importance.
51:2028:138456:12:11:86:556:594:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The dynamics are determined by Marshallian conditions if a natural advantage site loses its
51:2029:138547:11:12:69:557:583:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:innate importance. If local Marshallian forces are strong, agglomeration can persist absent the
51:2030:138642:12:12:69:557:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:original natural advantages. If local Marshallian forces are weak, the cluster may be vacated over
51:2031:138740:12:13:69:557:559:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time. The former scenario is in line with the related empirical work by Bleakley and Lin (2010) on
51:2032:138838:13:12:69:557:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the persistence of US cities originally centered on portage sites. This natural advantage has lost
51:2033:138936:12:12:69:557:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:its economic importance, but Bleakley and Lin (2010) Önd continued and growing importance
51:2034:139025:12:9:69:161:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of these locations.
51:2035:139044:9:11:86:556:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Looking ahead to future work, this framework provides a tractable setting for modelling
51:2036:139131:11:12:69:557:502:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:agglomeration patterns and industry evolution. As industries mature, their needs evolve and
51:2037:139222:12:11:69:557:490:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the concomitant maximal radii shift. A classic example is moving from heavy dependence upon
51:2038:139313:11:12:69:557:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:knowledge spillovers at industry birth to more production-centered factors at industry maturity.
51:2039:139409:12:11:69:557:467:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The associated changes in spillover lengths can be linked to dynamics in cluster patterns through
51:2040:139506:11:13:69:557:456:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this framework. Extending the model to have interesting interactions across industries could also
51:2041:139603:13:13:69:557:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a§ord evaluation of the role of diversity in industry birth similar to the work of Jacobs (1970)
51:2042:139699:13:37:69:233:430:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Duranton and Puga (2001).
51:2043:139728:37:17:69:275:393:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:Additional Theoretical Notes
51:2044:139756:17:16:86:556:376:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:-One can further introduce inter-industry Marshallian forces (coagglomeration) by adding
51:2045:139844:16:0:98:269:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a third term togj;A(i)of the form
51:2046:139877:0:10:272:285:369:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f13:P
51:2047:139878:10:8:296:312:359:6:g_d0_f16:6:g_d0_f16:i06=i;
51:2048:139884:8:0:286:322:351:6:g_d0_f16:6:g_d0_f12:A(i0)6=A(i)
51:2049:139895:0:20:326:556:360:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:GA(i)C(dj;j(i0)):An earlier version of this paper
51:2050:139944:20:13:98:556:340:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:traces out some of the properties that arise due to coagglomeration (e.g., the spatial scale
51:2051:140036:13:12:98:556:327:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of coagglomeration can exceed agglomeration even if the interaction e§ect is weaker). We
51:2052:140124:12:22:98:422:315:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:will pursue these coagglomeration traits further in future work.
51:2053:140188:22:11:86:556:293:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:-Our framework assumes that interaction costs exceed spillover beneÖts at some distance,
51:2054:140276:11:12:98:556:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with a single crossing property. While this condition holds in many settings, it is interest-
51:2055:140369:12:11:98:556:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing to note an empirical case where it does not. Ethnic networks have long been associated
51:2056:140459:11:13:98:556:259:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with reducing interaction costs at great distances and thereby facilitating economic ex-
51:2057:140547:13:12:98:556:246:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:changes (e.g., Rauch 2001, Kerr 2008). In e§ect, these networks transmit the beneÖts of
51:2058:140634:12:11:98:556:234:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:clusters that are typically conÖned spatially. Future extensions of this model could allow
51:2059:140724:11:22:98:372:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for networks, ethnic or otherwise, to connect clusters.
51:2060:140779:22:12:86:556:201:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:-In some industries, natural advantages are transmitted through contact with other Örms.
51:2061:140867:12:13:98:557:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:That is, if an industry-AÖrmihas access to a natural advantage sitek2K(A(i)), and
51:2062:140948:13:12:98:556:176:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:some other industry-AÖrmi0is proximate toj(i)but not tok, theni0derives some of the
51:2063:141031:12:13:98:556:164:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:beneÖt of the attraction sitek. Although a full treatment of such a model is outside the
51:2064:141119:13:13:98:556:151:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:scope of this paper, one special case stands out. IfGA(0) = 0and natural advantages are
51:2065:141206:13:12:98:557:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fully transmissible44, then Örms behave as in the case of Marshallian forces with attraction
51:2066:141298:12:11:98:556:126:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sites dictating the spatial distribution of Örm locations. In this case, agglomeration again
51:2067:141390:11:39:98:373:115:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increases with a longer maximal radius of interaction.
51:2068:141444:39:16:78:555:76:7:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f21:44We say that natural advantages arefully transmissibleif whenj(i0)2 B-A(j(i))anddj(i);k< -AK, theni0

52:2070:141630:0:26:69:240:699:17:g_d0_f32:17:g_d0_f32:Empirical Appendix
52:2071:141648:26:14:69:557:673:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:This appendix begins with a deeper presentation of the technology áow maps discussed in the
52:2072:141739:14:14:69:557:659:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:introduction. Color images of these maps are available at http://www.people.hbs.edu/wkerr/.
52:2073:141830:14:14:69:557:645:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We then introduce the US Census Bureau data employed and our approximation of the contin-
52:2074:141919:14:14:69:557:631:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:uous Duranton and Overman (2005) metric. We close with additional descriptive statistics on
52:2075:142010:14:31:69:428:617:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:US industrial concentration. The main text summarizes this material.
52:2076:142078:31:22:69:314:586:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:Technology Flows in Silicon Valley
52:2077:142112:22:14:69:557:564:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We start with a characterization of technology áows in Silicon Valley and its surrounding region.
52:2078:142209:14:14:69:557:550:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:The underlying structures of these technology áows exhibit several properties that are central
52:2079:142303:14:15:69:557:536:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to our location choice model, making this visual description a useful reference point. We employ
52:2080:142399:15:14:69:557:521:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:individual records of all patents granted by the United States Patent and Trademark O¢ ce
52:2081:142488:14:14:69:557:507:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:(USPTO) between January 1975 and May 2009 to inventors in the San Francisco Bay Area. We
52:2082:142576:14:14:69:557:493:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:deÖne the San Francisco Bay Area as any zip code that is within 75 miles of Redwood City, CA.
52:2083:142669:14:14:69:557:479:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Our analysis only considers industrial patents and the citations among them (e.g., we exclude
52:2084:142762:14:14:69:441:465:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:technology transfer from Stanford University). We exclude self-citations.
52:2085:142835:14:15:86:556:451:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We discuss in Section 3 the literature that exploits patent citations to measure knowledge
52:2086:142925:15:14:69:557:436:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:di§usion or technology spillovers. We use localized citations among patents to portray technology
52:2087:143022:14:14:69:557:422:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:sourcing zones at the zip code level within the San Francisco Bay Area. We assign Örms to zip
52:2088:143115:14:14:69:557:408:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:codes based on business directories and web-based searches.  This data development process
52:2089:143205:14:14:69:557:394:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:requires extensive manual e§ort as the San Francisco Bay Area produced as many industrial
52:2090:143294:14:14:69:557:380:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:patents over the last 30 years as the bottom 29 states combined. We thus map with certainty
52:2091:143385:14:15:69:557:366:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Örms that had two or more patents during the 1975-2009 period and use 20% subsamples for
52:2092:143473:15:14:69:557:351:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:assignees with just a single patent. In total, we obtain physical addresses for 88% of the potential
52:2093:143573:14:14:69:197:337:12:g_d0_f33:8:g_d0_f33:citations for our sample.1
52:2094:143599:14:14:86:556:323:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We start with the structure of technology áows in the core area of Silicon Valley and work
52:2095:143689:14:14:69:557:309:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:outwards.  App.  Figure 1a describes the core area that contains three-quarters of industrial
52:2096:143782:14:15:69:557:295:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:patents Öled from the San Francisco Bay Area. The core contains the top 10 zip codes in the
52:2097:143873:15:14:69:557:280:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:whole region in terms of patenting (and 18 of the top 25). We Örst place these 10 zip codes on
52:2098:143967:14:14:69:300:266:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the map and describe their technology zones.
52:2099:144011:14:14:86:556:252:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Panel A of App. Figure 1a shows the primary technology sourcing for zip code 95054, which
52:2100:144100:14:14:69:557:238:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:is marked with a star. This zip code produced the most industrial patents of any zip code in
52:2101:144192:14:14:69:557:224:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the San Francisco Bay Area (more than 20,000, which is equal to the seventeenth largest state).
52:2102:144287:14:15:69:557:210:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:It is home to Örms like Intel, Sun, Advanced Micro Devices, and Applied Materials. The other
52:2103:144379:15:14:69:539:195:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:points of the red shape are the three zip codes that Örms in 95054 cited most in their work.
52:2104:144471:14:14:86:556:181:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:These three zip codes contain about 30% of 95054ís external citations, with 95054 itself
52:2105:144559:14:17:69:557:167:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:accounting for about 15%. On average, the top three external zips contain 41% of local external
52:2106:144654:17:14:82:557:150:7:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:1Our approach has several limitations. First, the vast majority of web searches yield current business addresses.
52:2107:144767:14:9:69:557:136:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:In some cases, these searches also yield historical addresses for Örms that have been acquired or gone out of
52:2108:144876:9:10:69:557:127:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:business, but addresses are nonetheless more likely to be found for Örms currently in operation. Second, even
52:2109:144985:10:9:69:557:117:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:within the San Francisco Bay Area, some Örms have multiple facilities. In such cases, our top priority is for
52:2110:145094:9:10:69:557:108:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:locations where research is performed. Our results are robust when multiple assignments are possible to either
52:2111:145204:10:9:69:353:98:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:using the most likely facility or to weighting each facility equally.
52:2112:145273:9:10:79:557:89:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:A second source of address information comes from parallel work matching Örms into the Census Bureau data
52:2113:145378:10:10:69:557:79:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:described in Section 4 (e.g., Kerr and Fu 2008, Balasubramanian and Sivadasan 2010, Akcigit and Kerr 2010).
52:2114:145485:10:9:69:557:69:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:This approach produces a similar rank order of zip codes and description of cluster zones as those discussed
52:2115:145593:9:0:69:377:60:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:below. Disclosure restrictions prohibit further tabulating these results.
53:2116:145667:0:14:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:citations for a zip code. This dependency grows modestly as one moves from the core (39%) to
53:2117:145759:14:14:69:557:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the periphery (47%). Likewise, the relative importance of external citations within the focal zip

53:2120:146045:14:14:69:557:643:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:is greater than the more typical 10% share found at the metropolitan level due to both a larger

53:2127:146683:14:15:69:322:544:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and 95120 (e.g., IBM Almaden Research Center).
53:2128:146729:15:14:86:556:529:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Panels C and D show the top 6 and 10 zip codes, respectively. Although unrestricted in
53:2129:146815:14:14:69:557:515:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:design, the primary technology sourcing zones for each zip code in the core are also contained
53:2130:146909:14:14:69:557:501:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:in the core. This is true for all of the 18 zip codes in the core that are among the top 25. These
53:2131:147007:14:14:69:557:487:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:zones are characterized by small, overlapping regions that often exhibit directional transmission.

53:2145:148272:15:14:69:557:288:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:into the core. The green zone for Redwood City (ì2î) shifts up and encompasses Menlo Park
53:2146:148361:14:14:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and Palo Alto but less of the core. The black zone for South San Francisco (ì3î) further shifts
53:2147:148456:14:14:69:557:260:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:out and brushes the core. The northern side is similar. Fremontís pink zone extends deepest
53:2148:148547:14:14:69:557:246:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:through the core, while points further out attach more to the coreís edge. Finally, Santa Claraís
53:2149:148644:14:14:69:305:232:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:zone connects up the eastern edge of the core.
53:2150:148690:14:15:86:556:218:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:The background of the map demonstrates the roles of geographical features and transporta-
53:2151:148779:15:14:69:557:203:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tion costs. The shape of the core and outlying technology zones are dictated by mountains,
53:2152:148869:14:14:69:557:189:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:protected land, and the bay. Likewise, the edges of sourcing zones conform to major transporta-
53:2153:148964:14:14:69:557:175:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tion routes. Highway networks play a central role (e.g., horizontal áows across the top of the
53:2154:149058:14:14:69:557:161:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:core, vertical áows on the eastern edge of the core). Bridges help cross the bay. While not
53:2155:149149:14:14:69:557:147:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:shown in App. Figure 1a due to visual limitations, these same factors, especially the highway

53:2157:149315:15:14:86:556:118:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:The length of each zone is ináuenced by congestion. The distance along the upper edge of
53:2158:149403:14:14:69:557:104:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the orange zone from Menlo Park into the core is 14 miles with an estimated travel time of 28

53:2160:149590:14:0:69:557:76:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Park is 20 miles but with a comparable travel time of 32 minutes. A full spatial equilibrium
54:2161:149683:0:14:69:479:699:12:g_d0_f33:8:g_d0_f33:depends on additional factors like commercial and residential real estate prices.2

54:2169:150412:14:14:69:557:586:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Three zip codes from this group (i.e., Fremont, Hayward, and San Ramon) are also depicted

54:2174:150861:14:14:69:557:515:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:span. The importance of geography and transportation networks in shaping these zones is again
54:2175:150954:14:14:69:118:501:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:apparent.
54:2176:150963:14:14:86:556:487:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:This mapping exercise is a quick tour of the structure of technology áows in the San Fran-
54:2177:151053:14:14:69:557:473:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:cisco Bay Area. We Önd similar outcomes in unreported variants. Examples include using four
54:2178:151144:14:15:69:557:459:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:zip codes to deÖne technology sourcing zones, separating major technology groups, separating
54:2179:151236:15:14:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:entrants from long-lived incumbents, and examining only the most recent citations. More impor-
54:2180:151330:14:14:69:557:430:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tant for the development of our theory, Figure 1b in the main text shows similar patterns using
54:2181:151425:14:31:69:557:416:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:predominant commuting zones for scientists and engineers from the 2000 Census of Populations.
54:2182:151518:31:22:69:242:385:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:US Census Bureau Data
54:2183:151539:22:14:69:557:363:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Our estimates of industrial agglomeration patterns are developed through conÖdential data
54:2184:151628:14:14:69:557:349:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:housed by the US Census Bureau. The Longitudinal Business Database (LBD) provides an-
54:2185:151713:14:14:69:557:335:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:nual observations for every private-sector establishment with payroll from 1976 onward. The
54:2186:151804:14:15:69:557:321:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Census Bureau data are an unparalleled laboratory for studying the industrial structure of US
54:2187:151897:15:14:69:557:306:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Örms. Sourced from US tax records and Census Bureau surveys, the micro-records document
54:2188:151984:14:14:69:557:292:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the universe of establishments and Örms rather than a stratiÖed random sample or published
54:2189:152074:14:14:69:557:278:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:aggregate tabulations. In addition, the LBD lists physical locations of establishments rather
54:2190:152167:14:14:69:557:264:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:than locations of incorporation, circumventing issues related to higher legal incorporations in
54:2191:152262:14:15:69:174:250:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:states like Delaware.
54:2192:152283:15:14:86:556:235:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We deÖne industries through the three-digit level of the 1987 Standard Industrial ClassiÖ-
54:2193:152373:14:14:69:557:221:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:cation (SIC3). Industry assignment is at the establishment level for multi-unit Örms. We focus
54:2194:152467:14:14:69:557:207:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:on 362 SIC3 industries that are consistently measured from 1976 to 2001, after which time the
54:2195:152560:14:14:69:557:193:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:transition to the NAICS industry classiÖcations occurs. Our data contains 4.0 million estab-
54:2196:152652:14:14:69:557:179:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:lishments employing 68 million workers in 1977. In 1997, the data include 108 million workers
54:2197:152745:14:15:69:557:165:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and 5.8 million establishments. While we calculate agglomeration in all 26 years, our current
54:2198:152838:15:17:69:230:150:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:discussion focuses just on 1997.
54:2199:152870:17:15:82:557:133:7:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:2Glaeser (2008) provides a detailed introduction. Saiz (2010) demonstrates the linkage between geography
54:2200:152974:15:10:69:557:118:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:and city shape, and Baum-Snow (2007, 2010) studies the role of highways and transportation routes for city
54:2201:153080:10:0:69:100:108:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:shapes.
55:2202:153088:0:21:69:288:699:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:Duranton and Overman (2005)
55:2203:153115:21:15:69:557:678:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Duranton and Overman (2005, DO) construct a continuous metric of agglomeration. DO criticize
55:2204:153207:15:14:69:557:663:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:indices like Ellison and Glaeser (1997) that employ discrete spatial units (e.g., states) to measure
55:2205:153307:14:14:69:557:649:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:geographic concentration. This discreteness in e§ect makes the distance from Detroit, MI, to
55:2206:153399:14:14:69:557:635:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Chicago, IL, equivalent to that of Detroit, MI, to Miami, FL. The discreteness also fails to
55:2207:153491:14:14:69:557:621:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:account for within-geographic unit distances that arise, for example, due to Californiaís and
55:2208:153584:14:14:69:557:607:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Texasílarger spatial size relative to states within New England. DO instead propose analyzing
55:2209:153677:14:36:69:357:593:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:agglomeration of industryAthrough a continuous index
55:2210:153729:36:11:127:229:557:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f35:^KCtA(d)  =1

55:2235:153855:8:17:436:494:520:12:g_d0_f34:8:g_d0_f40:d-dj(i);j(i0)
