55:2239:153871:38:14:69:557:473:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:wheredj(i);j(i0)is the Euclidean distance between establishmentsiandi0within the focal industry
55:2240:153966:14:14:69:556:459:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f33:A. The functionfis a Gaussian kernel density function with bandwidthh. The summations
55:2241:154051:14:14:69:557:445:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:are over every pairwise bilateral distance of establishments within the industry analyzed (i.e.,
55:2242:154147:14:15:69:556:431:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f33:NA(NA-1)=2distances). The second formulation weights densities by establishment employ-
55:2243:154234:15:14:69:556:416:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:ments,e(i)ande(i0), while the top formulation focuses on plant counts regardless of size,e= 1.
55:2244:154328:14:14:69:510:402:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We exclude theCtandEmpsuperscripts in the main text and below for convenience.
55:2245:154406:14:14:86:556:388:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:These observed agglomeration densities are then compared to an underlying distribution of
55:2246:154495:14:14:69:557:374:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:economic activity. This baseline is calculated through 1000 draws of hypothetical industries of
55:2247:154590:14:14:69:556:360:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:equivalent size to the focal industryAand repeating the density estimation. An industry is said
55:2248:154685:14:15:69:556:346:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to be localized or dispersed at a given distancedwhen its observed agglomeration density shows
55:2249:154779:15:14:69:557:331:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:substantial deviation from the random draws. Our estimation procedure analyzes these local
55:2250:154869:14:14:69:557:317:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:departures in a systematic manner. DO likewise propose a global localization and dispersion
55:2251:154960:14:14:69:557:303:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:measure that captures sustained deviations up to a distance threshold speciÖed by the researcher.
55:2252:155057:14:31:69:389:289:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We discuss this measure after describing the base calculations.
55:2253:155120:31:22:69:239:258:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:Base Index Calculations
55:2254:155143:22:14:69:557:236:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Our approximations to the DO metric employ county-to-county distances to measure bilateral
55:2255:155233:14:14:69:557:222:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:distances between establishments.  The county spatial unit is the most detailed spatial unit
55:2256:155325:14:15:69:557:208:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:available for establishments in the LBD. We collapse establishment counts and employments
55:2257:155414:15:14:69:557:193:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:into a county-industry spatial distribution for each year. We then apply the almost ten mil-
55:2258:155506:14:14:69:557:179:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:lion potential pairwise distances between the 3141 counties.  We calculate distances between
55:2259:155598:14:14:69:557:165:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:county centroids using the Haversine áat-earth formula that abstracts from the earthís curva-
55:2260:155691:14:14:69:557:151:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:ture. Establishments in the same county are given a uniform distance of one mile. Multiple
55:2261:155781:14:14:69:557:137:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:factors yield conáicting recommendations regarding this latter choiceó for example, accounting
55:2262:155875:14:15:69:557:123:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:for larger land areas versus congestion e§ects with higher urban density. As shown below, the
55:2263:155968:15:14:69:557:108:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:major movements/tipping we analyze happen at distances of 50 miles or greater, making this
55:2264:156058:14:14:69:232:94:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:choice of secondary importance.
55:2265:156089:14:14:86:556:80:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:The combination of county-industry spatial distributions and county-to-county distances af-
55:2266:156180:14:0:69:557:66:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:fords a spatial distribution of establishments ranging from [same county] to just over 6,000 miles.
56:2267:156280:0:14:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We then apply the Gaussian kernel density functionfto smooth the distance series. For this
56:2268:156370:14:14:69:556:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:smoothing, the data are reáected around zero and the bandwidthhis chosen to minimize the
56:2269:156458:14:14:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:mean integrated squared error. This smoothed density function is calculated for both establish-
56:2270:156553:14:31:69:555:657:12:g_d0_f33:8:g_d0_f33:ment counts and employments. This process is repeated for each of the 362 industries annually.3
56:2271:156648:31:22:69:256:626:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:Local ConÖdence Intervals
56:2272:156673:22:14:69:557:604:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:These distance distributions are compared to counterfactuals of distances among randomly-
56:2273:156762:14:14:69:557:590:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:drawn establishments from the LBD. These counterfactual baselines control for the overall spatial
56:2274:156859:14:15:69:557:576:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:distribution of economic activity. Industries are deemed to be substantially agglomerated only
56:2275:156953:15:14:69:557:561:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to the extent they are more spatially clustered than US establishments generally. In preparing
56:2276:157047:14:14:69:557:547:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:this test, it is important that each counterfactual have a similar number of observations (and
56:2277:157141:14:14:69:557:533:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:therefore precision) as the focal distribution. It is also important, given the random nature of
56:2278:157237:14:14:69:557:519:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the establishment draw, to replicate the counterfactual baseline multiple times. DO converge on
56:2279:157332:14:14:69:443:505:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:1000 counterfactuals as the comparison for their agglomeration densities.
56:2280:157405:14:15:86:556:491:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Computational restrictions require that we simplify how the conÖdence bands are calculated.
56:2281:157496:15:14:69:557:476:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Our Örst simpliÖcation is that we only calculate conÖdence bands using data from 1977 and
56:2282:157585:14:14:69:557:462:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:1997, rather than annually as in the base index calculation above. These two years are chosen
56:2283:157678:14:14:69:557:448:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:as sample end points when economic censuses are conducted using the SIC system.  When
56:2284:157763:14:14:69:557:434:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:calculating our agglomeration measures, we Önd very similar patterns across all years 1976-2001
56:2285:157858:14:14:69:557:420:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:when using either the 1977 or 1997 baselines. Our current discussion focuses just on the 1977
56:2286:157951:14:15:69:475:406:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and 1997 cross-sections, and the conÖdence intervals are speciÖc to these years.
56:2287:158031:15:14:86:556:391:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Second, we approximate the establishment count in the industry. Industries di§er substan-
56:2288:158120:14:14:69:557:377:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tially in their establishment counts, ranging in 1997 from 18 industries having fewer than 100
56:2289:158214:14:14:69:557:363:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:establishments to 12 industries having more than 100,000. The maximum number of establish-
56:2290:158304:14:14:69:557:349:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:ments was over 400,000 for Eating and Drinking Places (581). It is computationally prohibitive
56:2291:158398:14:14:69:557:335:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to match exactly the establishment count in all industries and years. We thus randomly draw
56:2292:158489:14:15:69:557:321:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:without replacement 100,000 establishments for a hypothetical industry; this sampling is re-
56:2293:158581:15:14:69:284:306:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:peated 1000 times in both 1977 and 1997.
56:2294:158621:14:14:86:556:292:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We then calculate sub-draws of these samples using increments of 100 establishments from
56:2295:158709:14:14:69:557:278:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:a smallest industry size of 100 establishments up to 1500 establishments (i.e., 100, 200, ...,
56:2296:158803:14:14:69:557:264:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:1500). In addition, we calculate sub-draws using increments of 500 establishments from 1500
56:2297:158894:14:15:69:557:250:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:establishments to 5000 establishments and increments of 10,000 establishments up to 100,000
56:2298:158985:15:14:69:557:235:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:establishments. This procedure creates 32 comparable industry counts ranging from 100 estab-
56:2299:159077:14:14:69:557:221:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:lishments to 100,000 establishments.  As this procedure is repeated in two years and for 1000
56:2300:159170:14:14:69:557:207:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:samples, 64,000 random baselines are created. Industries are paired with constructed conÖdence
56:2301:159264:14:14:69:557:193:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:bands that most closely reáect the underlying observation counts (e.g., an industry with 223
56:2302:159356:14:14:69:459:179:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:establishments is compared to the conÖdence bands for 200 establishments).
56:2303:159430:14:15:86:556:165:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:To compute local conÖdence baselines akin to 5% and 95% conÖdence intervals, we apply
56:2304:159515:15:14:69:556:150:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the Gaussian kernel density functionfto smooth the 64,000 counterfactuals. For each distance,
56:2305:159608:14:14:69:557:136:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:we then identify the 50th and 950th extreme values in the smoothed series. We designate these
56:2306:159701:14:19:69:557:122:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:conÖdence intervals asKLCI-UA(d)andKLCI-LA(d). These local conÖdence intervals are speciÖc
56:2307:159791:19:13:82:557:103:7:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:3The largest values for pairwise distance are due to our inclusion of Alaska and Hawaii.  Densities are very
56:2308:159899:13:9:69:557:90:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:small at this level, however. We obtain equivalent results if pairwise establishment distances are capped at 3,000
56:2309:160013:9:10:69:557:81:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:miles, which is roughly the distance from Miami, FL, to Seattle, WA. The correlation for capped and uncapped
56:2310:160121:10:0:69:158:71:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:distributions is 0.99.
57:2311:160144:0:14:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to industries due to di§erences in industry size. While not expressed in the notation, the local
57:2312:160240:14:14:69:470:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:baselines are separately calculated for establishment counts and employments.
57:2313:160317:14:28:86:524:671:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Industry localization\rand dispersion at distancedare deÖned using the formulas:
57:2314:160396:28:0:176:256:643:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f35:\rA(d)-max
57:2315:160406:0:11:258:264:657:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:h
57:2316:160407:11:0:267:378:646:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f35:^KA(d)-KLCI-UA(d);0
57:2317:160426:0:14:378:384:657:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:i
57:2318:160427:14:25:541:556:643:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:(2)
57:2319:160430:25:0:183:256:618:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f35: A(d)-max
57:2320:160438:0:13:258:264:631:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:h
57:2321:160439:13:0:264:377:618:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f35:KLCI-LA(d)-^KA(d);0
57:2322:160458:0:13:377:383:631:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:i

57:2324:160471:20:25:238:323:598:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and0otherwise.
57:2325:160485:25:14:69:557:573:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:An industry is said to be neither localized nor dispersed at a given distance unless its density
57:2326:160581:14:25:69:502:559:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:falls outside of the 5% conÖdence bands. We also construct a combined index\rCA(d):
57:2327:160664:25:25:252:373:534:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f34:\rCA(d)-\rA(d)- A(d):
57:2328:160684:25:15:69:557:509:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:This index does not create a lower or upper bound for localization or dispersion but instead
57:2329:160776:15:14:69:557:494:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:views them symmetrically. This combined index is convenient for graphs and empirical analyses
57:2330:160869:14:31:69:478:480:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and continues to satisfy the necessary properties of an agglomeration estimator.
57:2331:160949:31:21:69:317:449:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:Global Localization and Dispersion
57:2332:160983:21:15:69:557:428:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Most industries exhibit local clustering or dispersion at one distance or another. The DO ap-
57:2333:161076:15:14:69:557:413:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:proach therefore also calculates indices of global localization and dispersion. These measures
57:2334:161170:14:14:69:557:399:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:quantify sustained deviations from the baselines of random placement.  The procedure Örst
57:2335:161259:14:14:69:466:385:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:speciÖes a distance threshold to analyze, and we denote this threshold asthr.
57:2336:161336:14:14:86:556:371:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:After deÖning the thresholdthr, the DO approach Örst looks for evidence of substantial
57:2337:161422:14:15:69:557:357:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:localization up to the threshold. If localization is not evident by the threshold, then evidence for
57:2338:161522:15:14:69:557:342:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:global dispersion is sought up to the threshold. If an industry is spatially distributed similarly to
57:2339:161623:14:14:69:557:328:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:overall economic activity, neither global localization nor dispersion will be found. This multi-step
57:2340:161723:14:14:69:557:314:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:procedure and omission of distances beyond the threshold is deÖned in this way since density
57:2341:161815:14:14:69:557:300:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:functions sum to one over the support. Thus, localization in one distance range will correspond
57:2342:161910:14:14:69:232:286:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to dispersion in other distances.
57:2343:161943:14:15:86:557:272:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Formally, the global indices of localization-and dispersion	are calculated using the for-
57:2344:162032:15:26:69:102:257:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:mulas:
57:2345:162038:26:0:148:207:231:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f37:-A(thr)-
57:2346:162046:0:18:217:246:242:12:g_d0_f41:8:g_d0_f36:Xthr
57:2347:162050:18:0:234:249:224:8:g_d0_f36:8:g_d0_f40:d=1
57:2348:162053:0:0:252:274:231:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f35:max
57:2349:162056:0:10:276:282:244:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:h
57:2350:162057:10:7:284:369:234:12:g_d0_f35:8:g_d0_f36:^KA(d)-KGCI-U
57:2351:162070:7:0:338:396:227:8:g_d0_f36:12:g_d0_f35:A;thr(d);0
57:2352:162080:0:13:396:402:244:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:i

57:2354:162084:27:0:155:207:204:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f37:	A(thr)-
57:2355:162092:0:18:217:246:215:12:g_d0_f41:8:g_d0_f36:Xthr
57:2356:162096:18:0:234:249:197:8:g_d0_f36:8:g_d0_f40:d=1
57:2357:162099:0:0:252:274:204:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f35:max
57:2358:162102:0:13:276:282:217:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:h
57:2359:162103:13:0:281:395:204:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f35:KGCI-LA;thr(d)-^KA(d);0
57:2360:162126:0:13:395:401:217:12:g_d0_f41:12:g_d0_f41:i
57:2361:162127:13:20:407:479:204:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f35:if-A(thr) = 0
57:2362:162140:20:25:221:305:184:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and0otherwise.
57:2363:162154:25:14:69:556:159:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f33:KGCI-UA;thr(d)andKGCI-LA;thr(d)are conÖdence baselines over distancesdfor measuring global lo-
57:2364:162248:14:14:69:557:145:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:calization and dispersion, respectively.  These global conÖdence intervals are wider than the
57:2365:162341:14:14:69:557:131:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:local conÖdence intervals calculated with the 50th and 950th extreme values for each distance.
57:2366:162435:14:15:69:556:117:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f33:KGCI-UA;thr(d)andKGCI-LA;thr(d)instead represent the local conÖdence values that when applied uni-
57:2367:162533:15:14:69:556:102:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:formly over the support[1;thr]results in 5% of the counterfactual baselines showing deviation
57:2368:162626:14:14:69:136:88:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:at both tails.
57:2369:162640:14:14:86:557:74:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Thus,KGCI-UA;thr(d)andKGCI-LA;thr(d)are speciÖc to the industry and threshold studied. The
57:2370:162730:14:0:69:557:60:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:global bands depend upon the industry studied as the counterfactual random draws replicate
58:2371:162821:0:14:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the number of establishments by industry.  Industries with fewer establishments have wider
58:2372:162911:14:14:69:557:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:conÖdence bands. While not included in DOís original formulation, the global bands also depend
58:2373:163005:14:14:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:on the threshold analyzed. ConÖdence bands are wider for longer intervals studied; equivalently,
58:2374:163101:14:14:69:426:657:12:g_d0_f33:8:g_d0_f33:the local conÖdence intervals become tighter with greater thresholds.4
58:2375:163171:14:14:86:556:643:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:When studying the UK, DO employ a distance threshold for identifying localization of 180
58:2376:163259:14:15:69:560:629:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:kilometers, which is the median distance among UK manufacturing establishments. The USí
58:2377:163346:15:14:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:large land mass and scattered regional industrial centers do not provide as clear of a threshold,
58:2378:163443:14:14:69:557:600:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and the appropriate threshold is not dictated by theory. There is also a question of edge e§ects
58:2379:163539:14:14:69:557:586:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:as discussed in Harrison and Kominers (2008). 1000 miles is approximately the median distance
58:2380:163632:14:14:69:557:572:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:between US establishments and is on the order of magnitude for the distance between Detroit,
58:2381:163724:14:14:69:557:558:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:MI, and Dallas, TX. The 25th, 10th, and 3rd percentiles of establishment bilateral distances are
58:2382:163820:14:15:69:557:544:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:approximately 500, 250, and 100 miles, respectively. These are on the order of magnitude of
58:2383:163911:15:14:69:485:529:12:g_d0_f33:8:g_d0_f33:Detroit, MI, to Washington, DC, Cincinnati, OH, and Lansing, MI, respectively.5
58:2384:163990:14:14:86:556:515:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:We therefore calculate global localization and dispersion across increments from 25 miles to
58:2385:164082:14:14:69:557:501:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:1000 miles. The 100 mile threshold is of comparable distance to the UK hurdle employed by DO
58:2386:164174:14:14:69:557:487:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:(180 kilometers = 112 miles), while 1000 miles maintains the median concept. Finally, we again
58:2387:164268:14:26:69:239:473:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:deÖne a combined index-CA(thr):
58:2388:164299:26:31:235:556:447:12:g_d0_f35:12:g_d0_f33:-CA(thr)--A(thr)-	A(thr):(4)
58:2389:164327:31:22:69:219:416:14:g_d0_f32:14:g_d0_f32:Descriptive Statistics
58:2390:164349:22:15:69:557:394:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Table 1A describes industrial concentration patterns in 1997 using global metrics.  Distance
58:2391:164441:15:14:69:557:379:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:thresholds increase from 50 miles in Panel A to 1000 miles in Panel E. Within each panel,
58:2392:164530:14:14:69:557:365:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the four rows document localization and dispersion using establishment counts. Localization is
58:2393:164624:14:14:69:557:351:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:typically higher in employment-weighted distributions than in those using plant counts (e.g.,
58:2394:164717:14:14:69:557:337:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Holmes and Stevens 2002); the pairwise correlation of our agglomeration statistics using counts
58:2395:164812:14:14:69:557:323:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and employment is 0.7. Employment-weighted distributions and estimates for 1977 are available
58:2396:164905:14:15:69:139:309:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:upon request.
58:2397:164918:15:14:86:556:294:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:To a distance threshold of 50 miles, a substantial number of industries show global localiza-
58:2398:165011:14:14:69:557:280:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tion or dispersion. Approximately 60% of industries display non-zero localization, while 30%
58:2399:165103:14:14:69:557:266:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:display non-zero dispersion. 10% of industries show zero global localization and dispersion, and
58:2400:165199:14:14:69:557:252:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:about 25% of industries show minimal deviation from the baseline economic activity of LBD
58:2401:165288:14:14:69:424:238:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:establishments (i.e., localization or dispersion values less than 0.001).
58:2402:165361:14:15:86:556:224:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:At Örst it may appear odd that 60% of industries are deemed globally localized when the
58:2403:165448:15:17:69:557:209:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:conÖdence bands are selected such that only 5% of the counterfactuals reach them.  This is
58:2404:165538:17:14:82:557:192:7:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:4Our procedure creates a grid of conÖdence bands by industry size and distance threshold for 1977 and 1997.
58:2405:165645:14:9:69:557:178:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:The industry sizes are the 32 interval ranges outlined earlier. We calculate exact global bands for eight thresholds
58:2406:165761:9:10:69:557:169:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:and use linear interpolation for distance thresholds between them. These eight thresholds and the extreme values
58:2407:165873:10:11:69:557:159:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:used for them are: 1000 miles (5th/995th), 500 (6/994), 375 (7/993), 250 (9/991), 175 (10/990), 100 (13/987),
58:2408:165982:11:11:69:557:148:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:75 (14/986), and 50 (18/982). As a comparison, DO also Önd that the 10/990 extreme values are appropriate
58:2409:166087:11:9:69:557:137:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:for 5% global conÖdence bands at a threshold of approximately 100 miles in their UK sample. These extreme
58:2410:166192:9:10:69:557:128:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:values are assigned through analyses of the complete distributions for the random draws of 100, 1000, 10,000,
58:2411:166301:10:9:69:557:118:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:and 100,000 establishments and are most representative for 1000 establishments. Appropriate extreme values
58:2412:166407:9:11:69:557:109:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:tend to widen (i.e., move to greater extremes) with large industry size due to the interaction of randomness and
58:2413:166519:11:8:69:499:98:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:greater distance granularity with more observations. Barlet et al. (2009) closely analyze this issue.
58:2414:166620:8:15:82:557:90:7:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:5More precisely, the percentiles of unweighted establishment distances in 1997 are 1013 miles (50th), 573
58:2415:166725:15:9:69:557:75:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:(25th), 280 (10th), and 106 (3rd). The 1977 percentiles are 967, 541, 259, and 95, respectively. Employment
58:2416:166832:9:0:69:310:66:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:weighted percentiles are shorter than count percentiles.
59:2417:166889:0:14:69:557:699:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to be expected if agglomeration forces exist, however, as the counterfactuals are built upon all
59:2418:166985:14:14:69:557:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:industrial establishments. The counterfactuals are not selected such that only 5% of industries
59:2419:167080:14:14:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:will be deemed agglomerated. This result is expected if, as in our model, sites are distributed
59:2420:167175:14:14:69:397:657:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:uniformly but agglomerative forces exist in nearly all industries.
59:2421:167241:14:14:86:556:643:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Moving from Panel A to Panel E, the share of industries that are localized and the values
59:2422:167330:14:15:69:557:629:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:of their localization increase as the distance threshold increases.  By 1000 miles, 88% of in-
59:2423:167424:15:14:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:dustries exhibit localization. Our combined metric (4) also increases in value four fold. This
59:2424:167518:14:14:69:557:600:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:is again despite the fact that the conÖdence intervals are being continually widened at longer
59:2425:167612:14:14:69:557:586:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:thresholds to maintain only 5% of the counterfactual series reaching them. This conÖrms the
59:2426:167703:14:14:69:557:572:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:modelís implication that an increase in the distance horizon should typically lead to increased
59:2427:167798:14:14:69:144:558:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:agglomeration.
59:2428:167812:14:15:86:556:544:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Unreported analyses Önd that these patterns also hold within each one-digit SIC sector up to
59:2429:167904:15:14:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:1000 miles. It is important to note, however, that global localization can decrease across some
59:2430:167999:14:14:69:557:515:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:distance ranges. For example, law o¢ ces can be concentrated at short distances within each city
59:2431:168095:14:14:69:557:501:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:but also present in many cities. A short threshold captures the initial spike. As the threshold
59:2432:168190:14:14:69:557:487:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:lengthens, the conÖdence intervals against which the densities are compared widen. This results
59:2433:168285:14:14:69:557:473:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:in a weaker measured concentration and, in some case, even a determination that the industry
59:2434:168377:14:15:69:245:459:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:is not globally concentrated at all.
59:2435:168413:15:14:86:556:444:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Table 1B describes the local deviations that are behind these patterns.  We also graph
59:2436:168499:14:14:69:557:430:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:in the main paper the fraction of industries that are localized at each distance level to 1000
59:2437:168593:14:14:69:557:416:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:miles. Localization is most powerful at short distance horizons, with substantial attenuation
59:2438:168686:14:14:69:557:402:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:commencing after 125 miles or so. Whereas about 60% of industries show localization at short
59:2439:168778:14:15:69:557:388:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:spatial scales, only 30% or thereabouts are localized at distances of 900-1000 miles. This pattern
59:2440:168876:15:14:69:557:373:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:is predicted in our model so long as some agglomerative force exists. Manufacturing industries
59:2441:168970:14:14:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:are more agglomerated at short spatial scales than non-manufacturing industries, a pattern that
59:2442:169065:14:14:69:557:345:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:reverses at longer horizons. This is to be expected given the transportable and tradeable nature
59:2443:169161:14:14:69:204:331:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:of manufactured products.
59:2444:169186:14:14:86:556:317:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Tables 2A-2D document extreme localization and dispersions values for 1997. Table 2A be-
59:2445:169274:14:15:69:557:303:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:gins with the global metric. Some industries are extremely localized regardless of the threshold
59:2446:169370:15:14:69:557:288:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:chosen. Most prominently, many of the tobacco, textiles, and apparel industries are very concen-
59:2447:169466:14:14:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:trated in the southeast of the US; moreover, these industries are very concentrated spatially at
59:2448:169562:14:14:69:557:260:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:small distances within this region. Other cases are due to very concentrated natural advantages
59:2449:169657:14:14:69:557:246:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:(e.g., mining industries) or idiosyncrasies in deÖnitions (e.g., freight transport on Great Lakes).
59:2450:169756:14:14:86:556:232:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:On the other hand, some industries are quite localized at small distances but have clusters
59:2451:169847:14:15:69:557:218:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:throughout the country. Many of the Önance industries and professional services, for example,
59:2452:169940:15:14:69:557:203:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:fall into this pattern. They have extreme values at small distances but not at larger distances.
59:2453:170036:14:14:69:557:189:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:A third pattern is where industries are not very locally clustered but tend to congregate in
59:2454:170128:14:14:69:557:175:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:one region of the US. This may again follow from natural advantages (e.g., regional oil and gas
59:2455:170223:14:14:69:518:161:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:deposits) or from Marshallian interactions among Örms (e.g., metalworking machinery).
59:2456:170308:14:14:86:556:147:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Table 2B similarly documents extreme dispersion values. The dispersed industries are intu-
59:2457:170398:14:15:69:557:133:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:itive. Many represent services and trade that require homogeneous distribution like gas stations,
59:2458:170495:15:14:69:557:118:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:hotels, hospitals, and utilities. Other dispersed industries like lumber and concrete are associated
59:2459:170595:14:14:69:557:104:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:with transportation of heavy products, which limits the advantages of even local agglomeration.
59:2460:170690:14:0:69:557:90:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:A third rationale is cheaper available land for dealers of used cars, mobile homes, and similar.
60:2461:170787:0:14:69:555:699:12:g_d0_f33:8:g_d0_f33:These purchases are substantial enough that consumers are willing to travel to the dealerships.6
60:2462:170883:14:14:86:556:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Tables 2C and 2D repeat this analysis using the localization metrics by distance. These tables
60:2463:170977:14:14:69:557:671:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:provide some simple intuition for the behavior described by our model. The localized concentra-
60:2464:171072:14:14:69:557:657:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tion and dispersion at 50 miles is naturally closely aligned with the global levels noticed earlier.
60:2465:171172:14:14:69:557:643:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Most of the localized industries at 50 miles, however, are among the most dispersed industries
60:2466:171266:14:15:69:557:629:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:when looking at concentric rings farther away. This is most easily seen in comparing the list of
60:2467:171362:15:14:69:557:614:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:highly localized industries at 50 miles to highly dispersed industries at 1000 miles. There are
60:2468:171457:14:14:69:557:600:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:also several cases of industries dispersed at short distances that show abnormal concentration
60:2469:171551:14:14:69:363:586:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:at moderate to longer distances horizons (e.g., hospitals).
60:2470:171610:14:14:86:556:572:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Industry movements across the panels can identify underlying forces of agglomeration and
60:2471:171698:14:14:69:557:558:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:their spatial scales. This behavior is embedded in global concentrations metrics, like Tables 2A
60:2472:171794:14:15:69:557:544:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and 2B, but is even more prominent in localized density functions. These local density functions
60:2473:171890:15:14:69:557:529:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:describe the edge of Örm location decisions in ways that aggregate agglomeration functions
60:2474:171980:14:14:69:491:515:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:obscure. This gradient or edge is the central piece that we study in the main text.
60:2475:172063:14:14:86:556:501:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Table 3A documents the correlation of the combined concentration metric (4) by threshold.
60:2476:172152:14:14:69:557:487:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:The correlation is very high among small thresholds and longer thresholds, but weaker in be-
60:2477:172244:14:14:69:557:473:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:tween. Index values using a 50 mile threshold have a 0.98 correlation with those using a 100 mile
60:2478:172341:14:15:69:557:459:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:threshold. The correlation of the 50 mile threshold to a 375 mile threshold, however, declines
60:2479:172435:15:14:69:557:444:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to 0.81. From here, the correlation only further declines to 0.73 when examining a 1000 mile
60:2480:172527:14:14:69:120:430:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:threshold.
60:2481:172537:14:14:86:556:416:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:Table 3B documents the correlation for local deviations. There is a much faster attenuation
60:2482:172628:14:14:69:557:402:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:of the correlation in local deviations across neighboring distances than for the global metric,
60:2483:172723:14:15:69:557:388:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:and a negative correlation exists for very distant values. These features are to be expected as
60:2484:172818:15:14:69:557:373:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:the underlying kernel densities sum to one over the support. Excess density in one distance
60:2485:172909:14:14:69:557:359:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:range yields below average density in another distance range. The non-linear summation be-
60:2486:172999:14:14:69:557:345:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:hind the global metric in Table 3A, however, will typically continue to identify an industry as
60:2487:173094:14:14:69:515:331:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:agglomerated at longer distance thresholds once it is agglomerated at lower thresholds.
60:2488:173181:14:14:86:557:317:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:The correlation between industry size and-CAis on the order of -0.1. Smaller industries are
60:2489:173272:14:15:69:557:303:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:typically slightly more localized. The adjustment of conÖdence bands insures that this is not due
60:2490:173369:15:14:69:557:288:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:to greater randomness in the series with fewer observations. It is more of an economic feature
60:2491:173463:14:14:69:557:274:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:that descends from why the industry has a small number of plants (e.g., economies of scale in
60:2492:173556:14:14:69:556:260:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:manufacturing versus consumer-oriented services). We have separately analyzed-CAvalues at
60:2493:173645:14:14:69:557:246:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:several thresholds for di§erent size industries. Growth in industry size is always associated with
60:2494:173743:14:14:69:556:232:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:declining-CAvalues; likewise, longer distance thresholds are associated with greater-CAvalues
60:2495:173836:14:126:69:163:218:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f33:in all size buckets.
60:2496:173856:126:13:82:557:92:7:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:6Tables 2A and 2B show evidence of agglomeration of production-related activities and dispersion of
60:2497:173955:13:10:69:557:79:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:distribution-related activities among some extreme industries. While Motion Picture Production and Services
60:2498:174062:10:9:69:557:69:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:(781) is extremely localized, Motion Picture Theaters (783) is quite dispersed. Other examples include textile
60:2499:174172:9:0:69:434:60:10:g_d0_f33:10:g_d0_f33:production versus clothing stores and gas and oil reÖnement versus service stations.

64:2581:179663:12:13:54:544:195:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:panels.  Within each panel, localization and dispersion statistics are calculated over observations displaying that trait.  The 
64:2582:179791:13:13:54:529:182:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:combined metric is calculated for all industries as the value of the localization metric minus the value of the dispersion 
64:2583:179914:13:12:54:529:169:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:metric.  The final row within each panel counts industries with approximately zero localization or dispersion.  The text 
64:2584:180035:12:0:54:255:157:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:further describes the construction of these metrics.
